Effect of Ruler's Dismissal on the Khateeb's Permission
Ruling on the khateeb's status when the ruler is dismissed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a khateeb's Friday prayer to remain valid when the appointing ruler is dismissed or a new ruler arrives, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving knowledge before versus after commencement.

Core Idea
A khateeb remains valid until official notice or new ruler arrives; ignorance before starting preserves validity.

This passage addresses a practical question: when a ruler is dismissed, do his appointed khateebs automatically lose their authority? The Hanafi answer clarifies that the khateeb's permission is tied to the office, not the person, and thus remains intact until the khateeb receives direct notification or the new ruler physically arrives. The ruling hinges on the khateeb's knowledge before starting the prayer, providing a clear distinction between ignorance and awareness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its conditions
State that the khateeb remains a deputy (na'ib) until one of two events occurs: (1) receipt of an official written dismissal, or (2) arrival of the new ruler. If neither happens before the prayer starts, the prayer is valid.
2
Distinguish knowledge before and after starting
If the khateeb knows of the dismissal before commencing the prayer, his prayer is void (batil). If he learns after starting, the prayer remains valid because the commencement was sound.
The principle: 'Shurūʿuhu ṣaḥḥa' (his commencement was valid).
3
Note the analogy with the imam's appointment
The text draws an analogy: if an imam appoints someone to lead prayer and then places a legal impediment (ḥajar) on him during the prayer, the prayer continues unaffected. This reinforces that the ruling depends on the time of knowledge.
4
Apply the ruling to the example of the Pasha in Egypt
The commentator states that if the Pasha (governor) is dismissed, the khateebs remain in their positions and do not need new permission from the successor unless they are specifically dismissed.
This illustrates the general principle that officials remain until formally removed.
5
Extract the general principle
The core principle: a delegated authority remains valid until the delegate receives explicit notification of termination or the new principal physically assumes authority, provided the delegate has no knowledge before acting.

Source Text

He remains a deputy, but they stipulated that the written order of his dismissal must come to him, or the second ruler must arrive. If either of these occurs, his prayer is void. If he prays while the condition is still intact, it is permissible because their officials remain in their positions until they are dismissed. Thus in al-Khulasa. And by this it is known that if the Pasha in Egypt is dismissed, the khateebs remain in their positions and do not need new permission from the second (ruler) unless he dismisses them. And we restricted it to his knowledge of the dismissal before commencing, because if he commenced and then another ruler arrived, he continues in his prayer, like a man whom the imam appointed to lead the people in Friday prayer and then placed a legal impediment upon him while he is in prayer, it does not affect him. Because his commencement is valid. If the impediment occurred before commencement, it takes effect.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It discusses the status of a deputy imam or khateeb when the appointing ruler is dismissed or a new ruler arrives. The key condition is that the deputy remains in authority until he receives the official letter of dismissal or the new ruler physically arrives. If he leads the Friday prayer without knowledge of either event, his prayer is valid because officials continue in their posts until formally removed. The example of the Pasha in Egypt illustrates that the appointment of the khateeb is tied to the office of the ruler, not his person; thus, the khateeb remains until specifically notified. If the khateeb begins the prayer and then a new ruler arrives, he continues validly since his commencement was sound. However, if he knows of the dismissal before starting, his prayer would be void. This shows that the ruling hinges on actual knowledge or notification.

Key Terms
الكتاب بعزله (al-kitāb bi-ʿazlihi): The official written document of dismissal sent to the deputy
الأمير الثاني (al-amīr al-thānī): The new ruler who arrives and supercedes the previous one

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The khateeb's permission continues until he receives official notification or the new ruler arrives; knowledge before starting is key to validity.

Friday Prayer Time Exit: Nafl or Void?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the consequence of time exit in Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of Friday prayer when Dhuhr time exits, and identify the mufta bihi opinion.

Core Idea
If Dhuhr time exits during Friday prayer, it becomes void entirely (Sahibayn) – not nafl.

Friday prayer must be performed within the time of Dhuhr. But what happens if the time expires while the prayer is still in progress? The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer transforms into a voluntary (nafl) prayer, while his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), maintain that it becomes completely void. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the dispute and clarifies the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the time condition
Identify that Friday prayer is valid only within Dhuhr time. The matn says 'wa waqt al-dhuhr' indicating this is a condition (shart).
The Prophet (peace be upon him) never prayed Friday outside Dhuhr time.
2
Identify the problem scenario
What if Dhuhr time exits while the prayer is being performed? The text considers this situation, even if the worshipper has already sat for tashahhud.
The exit of time is absolute; it does not matter when it exits.
3
Present Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa says it turns into a voluntary prayer (translates as 'tanqalibu tatawwu'an'). His reasoning: the essence of the prayer is valid; only the description of Friday is lost, so it reverts to nafl.
This is based on the principle that when the specific description fails, the general act remains valid.
4
Present the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it becomes void entirely (yabtulu aslan). Their reasoning: the intention was for Friday, which is invalid, so the whole prayer is invalid. They do not allow a change of intention mid-prayer.
The text notes that Abu Yusuf here contradicts his own principle that when the description is void, the essence does not become void.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator indicates the view from al-Muhit (which aligns with the Sahibayn) is stronger, and the view from al-Nawadir (which might support Abu Hanifa) is considered weak. Thus the mufta bihi is that the Friday prayer is void.
Practical consequence: one must stop and pray Dhuhr later; the prayer does not count as nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ووقت الظهر ) أي شرط صحتها أن تؤدى في وقت الظهر فلا تصح قبله ولا بعده لأن شرعية الجمعة مقام الظهر على خلاف القياس لأنه سقوط أربع بركعتين فتراعي الخصوصيات التي ورد الشرع بها مما لم يثبت دليل على نفي اشتراطها ولم يصلها عليه السلام خارج الوقت في عمره ولا بدون الخطبة فيه فيثبت اشتراطهما وكون الخطبة في الوقت بخلاف ما قام الدليل على عدم اشتراطه ككونها خطبتين بينهما جلسة إلى غير ذلك مما هو مسنون أو واجب كما سيأتي بيانه قوله فتبطل يخروجه أي صلاة الجمعة بخروج وقت الظهر ولو بعد القعود قدر التشهد لفوات شرطها فلا يبني الظهر لاختلاف الصلاتين قدراً وحالاً واسماً. أطلقه فشمل كل مصل لها ولهذا قال في المحيط : لو نام خلف الإمام في الجمعة ولم ينتبه حتى خرج الوقت فسدت صلاته لأنه لو أتم لصار قاضياً وقضاء الجمعة في غير وقتها لا يجوز، ولو انتبه في الوقت لم تفسد لأنه صار مؤدياً للجمعة في وقتها اهـ. وفي تهذيب القلانسي من باب المواقيت وفي الجمعة لو خرج وقت الظهر تنقلب تطوعاً عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما يبطل أصلاً .اهـ. ولا يخفى مخالفة أبي يوسف أصله هنا فإنه موافق للإمام في أنه إذا بطل الوصف لا تبطل الأصل وفي السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى النوادر: إمام صلى بالناس الجمعة فدخل معه رجل في الصلاة فزحمه الناس فلم يستطع الركوع والسجود حتى فرغ الإمام ودخل وقت العصر، فإنه يتم الجمعة بغير قراءة بخلاف ما لو كان في الفجر والمسألة بحالها ثم طلعت الشمس حيث تفسد صلاته لعدم مصادفة الوقت، وينبغي أن يكون ما في النوادر ضعيفاً لأن ما في المحيط يخالفه لأنه لا فرق في اللاحق بين أن يكون عذره النوم أو الزحمة
His saying: (And the time of Dhuhr) means that its validity condition is that it be performed in the time of Dhuhr, so it is not valid before it nor after it, because the legislation of Friday in place of Dhuhr is contrary to analogy, because it is dropping four (rak'ahs) for two, so the specificities that the Law has brought are observed, for which no evidence has been established to negate their conditionality. And he (peace be upon him) never performed it outside the time in his life, nor without the khutbah. Thus the conditionality of both is established, and that the khutbah be in the time, contrary to what evidence has been established for its non-conditionality, such as it being two sermons with a sitting between them, etc., which are sunnah or wajib, as will be explained. His saying: 'so it becomes void by its exit' means that the Friday prayer becomes void by the exit of the time of Dhuhr, even after the sitting (qada) of the tashahhud, because its condition is lost. So he does not build (qada') for Dhuhr, due to the difference between the two prayers in quantity, state, and name. He gave it absolutely, so it includes every person performing it. For this, al-Muhit said: If someone sleeps behind the imam in Friday prayer and does not wake up until the time exits, his prayer is invalid, because if he completed he would become a qadi (making up), and making up Friday outside its time is not permissible. If he wakes up within the time, it is not invalid because he becomes an adā' (performer) of Friday in its time. In Tahdhib al-Qalanisi, from the chapter of times, and in Friday, if the time of Dhuhr exits, it turns into a voluntary prayer according to Abu Hanifa, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it becomes void entirely. It is not hidden that Abu Yusuf contradicts his own principle here, for he agrees with the Imam that when the description becomes void, the essence does not become void. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, attributed to al-Nawadir: 'An imam led the people in Friday prayer, and a man entered the prayer with him, but the people crowded him so he could not bow or prostrate until the imam finished and the time of Asr entered. He then completes the Friday prayer without recitation, contrary to the case of Fajr if the same situation occurs and the sun rises, where his prayer becomes void due to lack of coinciding with the time.' It should be that what is in al-Nawadir is weak, because what is in al-Muhit contradicts it, for there is no difference for the latecomer between his excuse being sleep or crowding.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a ruling with proof. The matn states 'ووقت الظهر' – that Friday prayer must be within Dhuhr time. The commentator explains that this is a condition (shart), and if the time exits, the prayer is invalid. The proof is from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who never prayed Friday outside its time. The commentary then addresses what happens if time exits during prayer: according to Abu Hanifa, it turns into a voluntary (nafl) prayer because the essence of the prayer is valid, only the description of Friday is lost. But according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the entire prayer becomes void. The commentator notes that Abu Yusuf here contradicts his own principle that if the description is void, the essence does not become void. A case from al-Muhit: if someone sleeps through the prayer and misses the time, his Friday is invalid. A case from al-Nawadir about a latecomer who cannot bow due to crowding after the time exits is considered weak because al-Muhit treats both sleep and crowding the same. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows al-Muhit, confirming the voidness of Friday outside its time.

Key Terms
انقلاب تطوعاً (inqilāb taṭawwuʿan): The transformation of the Friday prayer into a voluntary (nafl) prayer when the time exits
يبطل أصلاً (yabṭulu aṣlan): The prayer becomes completely void, not even counting as nafl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) opinion in the Hanafi school, what happens to Friday prayer if the time of Dhuhr exits before the prayer is completed?
A) It becomes a voluntary (nafl) prayer
B) It remains valid as Friday
C) It becomes completely void
D) It is completed as Dhuhr prayer

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that Friday prayer is void if Dhuhr time exits, so one must pray Dhuhr later.

The Khutbah: Timing and Congregation Requirement
Ruling with proof on khutbah conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two timing conditions of the khutbah and identify the internal Hanafi dispute on the number of listeners required.

Core Idea
The khutbah must precede the prayer and be within Dhuhr time, but whether the khateeb needs an audience is disputed.

The khutbah is a necessary condition for Friday prayer. This lesson focuses on two key conditions: its timing and the presence of a congregation. While the khutbah must precede the prayer and occur during Dhuhr time, scholars differ on whether the khateeb must have at least one listener. We'll explore the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing condition
Find in the passage where it states that the khutbah must be before the prayer and within Dhuhr time. Note the phrases: 'وشرط صحتها الخطبة وكونها قبل الصلاة' and 'ولو قال فيه أي في وقت الظهر لكان أولى'.
The condition is that the khutbah must be before the prayer and during Dhuhr time; if given before Dhuhr, the prayer is invalid.
2
Locate the proof for timing
The passage cites the Prophet's constant practice: 'النبي ما صلاها دون الخطبة' and consensus in Fath al-Qadir on the conditionality of the khutbah itself.
The proof is both sunnah (Prophetic practice) and ijma.
3
Examine the congregation condition and its dispute
The passage presents different views: the commentator stipulates a congregation even if deaf or asleep (apparently not one); al-Khulasa says alone is invalid; al-Asl reports two narrations; Fath al-Qadir permits alone; al-Zahiriyya prohibits.
The dispute is whether the khateeb needs at least one listener. Fath al-Qadir's view is permissibility; al-Zahiriyya corrects it to impermissibility.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view per Fath al-Qadir is that the khateeb alone is permissible, but caution is advised. The practical consequence: prayer is valid if khateeb is alone, but to avoid dispute, at least one listener is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والخطبة (قبلها أي و شرط صحتها الخطبة وكونها قبل الصلاة لما قدمناه النبي ما صلاها دون الخطبة. ونقل في فتح القدير الإجماع على اشتراط نفس الخطبة ولأنها شرط وشرط الشيء سابق عليه، ولو قال فيه أي في وقت الظهر لكان أولى لأنه شرط حتى لو خطب قبله وصلى فيه لم تصح . وشرط الشارح أن يكون بحضرة جماعة تنعقد بهم الجمعة وإن كانوا صماً أو نياماً وظاهره أنه لا يكفي لوقوعها الشرط حضور واحد. وفي الخلاصة ما يخالفه فإنه قال : لو خطب وحده ولم يحضره أحد لا يجوز. وفي الأصل قال : فيه روايتان. ولو حضر واحد أو اثنان وخطب وصلى بالثلاثة جاز، ولو خطب بحضرة يجز إن كن وحدهن انتهى. وفي فتح القدير : المعتمد أنه لو خطب وحده فإنه يجوز أخذاً . قولهم يشترط عنده . في التسبيحة والتحميدة أن يقال على قصد الخطبة، فلو حمد العطاس لا يجزئ عن الواجب .انتهى. وفيه نظر ظاهر لأنه لا يدل على ما ذكره بشيء من أنواع الدلالات كما لا يخفى وصحح في الظهيرية أنه لو خطب وحده فإنه لا يجوز. وفي المضمرات معزياً إلى الزاد: وهل تقوم الخطبة مقام الركعتين؟ اختلف المشايخ منهم من قال تقوم ولهذا لا تجوز إلا بعد دخول الوقت، ومنهم من قال لا تقوم وهو الأصح لأنه لا يشترط لها سائر شروط من استقبال القبلة والطهارة وغير لك انتهى. وفي البدائع ثم وهي وإن كانت قائمة مقام الركعتين شرط وليست بركن لأن صلاة الجمعة لا تقام بالخطبة فلم تكن من أركانها اهـ . وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن الخطبة شرط الانعقاد في حق من ينشئ التحريمة للجمعة لا في حق كل من صلاها واشتراط حضور الواحد أو الجمع ليتحقق معنى الخطبة لأنها من النسبيات فعن هذا قالوا : لو أحدث الإمام فقدم من لم يشهدها جاز أن يصلي بهم الجمعة لأنه بان تحريمته على تلك التحريمة المنشأة، فالخطبة شرط انعقاد الجمعة في حق من ينشيء التحريمة فقط، ألا ترى إلى صحتها من المقتدين الذين لم يشهدوا الخطبة؟ فعلى هذا كان القياس فيما لو أفسد هذا الخليفة أن لا يجوز أن يستقبل بهم الجمعة لكنهم استحسنوا جواز استقباله لهم لأنه لما قام مقام الأول التحق به حكماً، فلو فسد الأول استقبل الثاني، فلو كان الأول أحدث قبل الشروع فقدم من لم يشهد الخطبة لا يجوز أهـ. ولم يشترط المصنف أنه يصلي عقب الخطبة بلا تراخ، ففيه أشار إلى أنه ليس بشرط فلذا قالوا : إن الخطبة تعاد على وجه الأولوية لو تذكر الإمام فائتة في صلاة الجمعة ولو كانت الوتر حتى فسدت
His saying: (and the khutbah before it) means that its validity condition is the khutbah and its being before the prayer, because we have mentioned that the Prophet never prayed it without the khutbah. And it is transmitted in Fath al-Qadir that there is consensus on the conditionality of the khutbah itself, and because it is a condition, and the condition of a thing precedes it. If he said 'in it' meaning in the time of Dhuhr, it would be better, because it is a condition such that if he gives the khutbah before it (the time) and prays in it, it is not valid. And the commentator stipulated that it be in the presence of a congregation that would hold Friday prayer with them, even if they are deaf or asleep, and its apparent meaning is that the presence of one is not sufficient for the condition to occur. In al-Khulasa, there is what contradicts it, for it said: 'If he gives the khutbah alone and no one attends, it is not permissible.' In al-Asl, it is said there are two narrations. 'If one or two attend and he gives the khutbah and prays with the three, it is permissible. And if he gives the khutbah in the presence of women alone it is not permissible.' End. In Fath al-Qadir: 'The relied-upon is that if he gives the khutbah alone, it is permissible, taking their statement that it is required for it to be with the intention of the khutbah. If someone sneezes and praises Allah, it does not suffice for the obligation.' End. And there is an apparent flaw in it, because it does not indicate what he mentioned by any type of indication, as is not hidden. And it is corrected in al-Zahiriyya that if he gives the khutbah alone, it is not permissible. In al-Mudmarat, attributed to al-Zad: 'Does the khutbah stand in place of the two rak'ahs? The mashayikh differed. Some said it does, and for this it is not permissible except after the entry of time. Some said it does not, and this is sahih because its conditions do not include all the conditions of prayer like facing the qibla and purity etc.' End. In al-Bada'i: 'Then, even though it stands in place of the two rak'ahs, it is a condition and not a pillar, because the Friday prayer is not established by the khutbah, so it is not from its pillars.' End. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that the khutbah is a condition for the validity of the Friday prayer with respect to the one who initiates the tahrimah for Friday, not with respect to everyone who prays it. The condition of the presence of one or a group is to realize the meaning of the khutbah because it is from relative matters. For this they said: If the imam nullifies his wudu and then sends forward someone who did not attend the khutbah, it is permissible for him to lead them in Friday prayer because his tahrimah is built upon that initiated tahrimah. Thus the khutbah is a condition for the validity of Friday only for the one who initiates the tahrimah. Do you not see the validity of the prayer for those followers who did not attend the khutbah? So on this basis, in the case where this khalif (successor) invalidates (the prayer), the analogy would be that he should not be allowed to start the Friday prayer for them, but they (the scholars) deemed it good (istihsan) for him to start it because since he takes the place of the first, he is annexed to him by rule. So if the first is invalidated, the second starts it. If the first had invalidated (wudu) before commencement, then he sends forward someone who did not attend the khutbah, it is not permissible.' End. And the author did not stipulate that he pray immediately after the khutbah without delay, so in this there is an indication that it is not a condition, and therefore they said: 'The khutbah is repeated on the basis of priority if the imam remembers an outstanding prayer during the Friday prayer, even if it is witr, such that it becomes invalid.'
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining that the khutbah is a condition for Friday prayer, based on the Prophet's consistent practice. The commentary discusses several sub-issues: (1) The khutbah must be before the prayer and within Dhuhr time. (2) A congregation is required, but the number is disputed: some say a single person suffices, others require at least three. The relied-upon view in Fath al-Qadir allows the khateeb giving khutbah alone, but al-Zahiriyya rules it impermissible. (3) The khutbah is a condition (shart) not a pillar (rukn) because the prayer can be valid without it for followers who join late or are appointed after the khutbah. (4) If the imam becomes invalid (e.g., nullifies wudu), his substitute can lead if he heard the khutbah; otherwise not. (5) There is no condition of immediate connection between khutbah and prayer. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving rules from prophetic practice and scholarly consensus, and it resolves internal disputes by preferring the majority or relied-upon view.

Key Terms
شرط الانعقاد (sharṭ al-inʿiqād): A condition for the validity of the Friday prayer specifically for the one who initiates the tahrimah (opening takbir), not for followers
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer; a condition for its validity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the effect of giving the khutbah before Dhuhr time?
A) The khutbah is still valid, but the prayer must be after Dhuhr
B) The khutbah is invalid, so the prayer is invalid
C) The khutbah is valid, but it must be repeated after Dhuhr
D) The khutbah is valid and the prayer is valid if within Dhuhr time

Key Takeaway
The khutbah is a conditioned condition: it must precede the prayer and be within Dhuhr time, and at least one listener is recommended to avoid dispute.

The Khutbah as Condition (Shart) Not Pillar (Rukn) and Its Scope
Ruling with proof on legal nature and scope of khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies the khutbah as a condition (shart) rather than a pillar (rukn), and identify that it is a condition only for the one initiating the tahrimah.

Core Idea
The khutbah is a condition for the imam, not for followers, and it is not a pillar because the prayer is not established by it.

A crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh is between a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn). This lesson focuses on the passage where the author explicitly states that the khutbah is a condition, not a pillar, because the Friday prayer is not established by the khutbah. It further clarifies that this condition applies only to the person who initiates the tahrimah (the imam), not to followers, as evidenced by the ruling on a substitute imam who did not attend the khutbah. We will also explore the istihsan ruling for the substitute and the absence of an immediate connection requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement that khutbah is a condition, not a pillar
Find the quote from al-Bada'i: 'وهي وإن كانت قائمة مقام الركعتين شرط وليست بركن'. Understand the reasoning: because the Friday prayer is not established by the khutbah (صلاة الجمعة لا تقام بالخطبة).
Even though the khutbah stands in place of two rak'ahs, it is not a pillar.
2
Understand the scope: condition for the one initiating tahrimah
From Fath al-Qadir: 'الخطبة شرط الانعقاد في حق من ينشئ التحريمة للجمعة لا في حق كل من صلاها'. This means it is only required for the imam who starts the prayer, not for followers.
Followers who miss the khutbah still pray validly.
3
Analyze the istihsan ruling for the substitute imam
If the original imam nullifies wudu after the khutbah, he can appoint a substitute who did not attend the khutbah. Analogy (qiyas) would require attendance, but istihsan permits it because the substitute is annexed to the original.
This shows the condition is tied to the original initiator.
4
Note the lack of immediate connection condition
The author did not stipulate that prayer must follow immediately after the khutbah. The passage gives an example: if the imam remembers an outstanding prayer, the khutbah is repeated as a priority, implying no requirement of immediate succession.
This supports the view that the khutbah is a condition, not a pillar.

Source Text

حتى فسدت
His saying: (and the khutbah before it) means that its validity condition is the khutbah and its being before the prayer, because we have mentioned that the Prophet never prayed it without the khutbah. And it is transmitted in Fath al-Qadir that there is consensus on the conditionality of the khutbah itself, and because it is a condition, and the condition of a thing precedes it. If he said 'in it' meaning in the time of Dhuhr, it would be better, because it is a condition such that if he gives the khutbah before it (the time) and prays in it, it is not valid. And the commentator stipulated that it be in the presence of a congregation that would hold Friday prayer with them, even if they are deaf or asleep, and its apparent meaning is that the presence of one is not sufficient for the condition to occur. In al-Khulasa, there is what contradicts it, for it said: 'If he gives the khutbah alone and no one attends, it is not permissible.' In al-Asl, it is said there are two narrations. 'If one or two attend and he gives the khutbah and prays with the three, it is permissible. And if he gives the khutbah in the presence of women alone it is not permissible.' End. In Fath al-Qadir: 'The relied-upon is that if he gives the khutbah alone, it is permissible, taking their statement that it is required for it to be with the intention of the khutbah. If someone sneezes and praises Allah, it does not suffice for the obligation.' End. And there is an apparent flaw in it, because it does not indicate what he mentioned by any type of indication, as is not hidden. And it is corrected in al-Zahiriyya that if he gives the khutbah alone, it is not permissible. In al-Mudmarat, attributed to al-Zad: 'Does the khutbah stand in place of the two rak'ahs? The mashayikh differed. Some said it does, and for this it is not permissible except after the entry of time. Some said it does not, and this is sahih because its conditions do not include all the conditions of prayer like facing the qibla and purity etc.' End. In al-Bada'i: 'Then, even though it stands in place of the two rak'ahs, it is a condition and not a pillar, because the Friday prayer is not established by the khutbah, so it is not from its pillars.' End. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that the khutbah is a condition for the validity of the Friday prayer with respect to the one who initiates the tahrimah for Friday, not with respect to everyone who prays it. The condition of the presence of one or a group is to realize the meaning of the khutbah because it is from relative matters. For this they said: If the imam nullifies his wudu and then sends forward someone who did not attend the khutbah, it is permissible for him to lead them in Friday prayer because his tahrimah is built upon that initiated tahrimah. Thus the khutbah is a condition for the validity of Friday only for the one who initiates the tahrimah. Do you not see the validity of the prayer for those followers who did not attend the khutbah? So on this basis, in the case where this khalif (successor) invalidates (the prayer), the analogy would be that he should not be allowed to start the Friday prayer for them, but they (the scholars) deemed it good (istihsan) for him to start it because since he takes the place of the first, he is annexed to him by rule. So if the first is invalidated, the second starts it. If the first had invalidated (wudu) before commencement, then he sends forward someone who did not attend the khutbah, it is not permissible.' End. And the author did not stipulate that he pray immediately after the khutbah without delay, so in this there is an indication that it is not a condition, and therefore they said: 'The khutbah is repeated on the basis of priority if the imam remembers an outstanding prayer during the Friday prayer, even if it is witr, such that it becomes invalid.'
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining that the khutbah is a condition for Friday prayer, based on the Prophet's consistent practice. The commentary discusses several sub-issues: (1) The khutbah must be before the prayer and within Dhuhr time. (2) A congregation is required, but the number is disputed: some say a single person suffices, others require at least three. The relied-upon view in Fath al-Qadir allows the khateeb giving khutbah alone, but al-Zahiriyya rules it impermissible. (3) The khutbah is a condition (shart) not a pillar (rukn) because the prayer can be valid without it for followers who join late or are appointed after the khutbah. (4) If the imam becomes invalid (e.g., nullifies wudu), his substitute can lead if he heard the khutbah; otherwise not. (5) There is no condition of immediate connection between khutbah and prayer. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving rules from prophetic practice and scholarly consensus, and it resolves internal disputes by preferring the majority or relied-upon view.

Key Terms
شرط الانعقاد (sharṭ al-inʿiqād): A condition for the validity of the Friday prayer specifically for the one who initiates the tahrimah (opening takbir), not for followers
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer; a condition for its validity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, to whom does the condition of the khutbah apply?
A) Every person who prays Jumu'ah
B) Only the imam who initiates the tahrimah
C) Only those who arrive late
D) Only the substitute imam

Key Takeaway
The khutbah is a condition for the initiator of the Friday prayer, not for followers, and its absence does not affect those who join late.

Salah — Prayer

Does the Friday Khutbah Require an Audience? The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of hudur for khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon position on the minimum attendees for the Friday khutbah and explain the evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah is valid with one listener – the condition is the utterance of dhikr, not a crowd.

The Friday khutbah (sermon) is a central element of Jumu'ah prayer. Among Hanafi jurists, there is a dispute whether the presence of an audience is a necessary condition for its validity. Some authorities require at least a group, while the relied-upon position holds that even one person suffices. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind both views and the practical implications for the Friday prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether 'hudur' (presence) of attendees is a condition (shart) for the validity of the khutbah. The source text presents two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
The issue is intra-Hanafi; other schools have different requirements (e.g., 40 in Shafi'i).
2
Understand the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
In al-Asl, there are two narrations: one requiring at least one person, another allowing the khatib to deliver the khutbah alone. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) accepts the narration that one person suffices.
The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) seems to indicate that one person is insufficient, but this is not the final position.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
The Quranic verse (62:9) commands 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah'. 'Dhikr' is interpreted as the khutbah, and the Hanafi school argues that any speech of dhikr suffices, regardless of the number of listeners. The term 'khutbah' linguistically means any address, not necessarily to a crowd.
This argument overrides the custom that a khutbah is usually delivered to a group.
4
Examine the practical implications (furu')
The text discusses various branches: if the imam becomes impure, a substitute who did not hear the khutbah can lead; if the interval between khutbah and prayer is long, the khutbah must be repeated; a minor can deliver the khutbah but an adult must lead the prayer.
These rulings stem from the principle that the khutbah is a condition for the one initiating the tahrimah, not for followers.

Book of Prayer, Chapter of Friday Prayer. The prayer for those who leave Friday prayer? Even if they were deaf or sleeping, and its apparent meaning is that the presence of one is not sufficient for the condition of its occurrence. In al-Khulasah, there is what contradicts it, for he said: If he delivered the khutbah alone and no one attended it, it is not permissible. In al-Asl, he said: there are two narrations. If one or two attended and he delivered the khutbah and prayed with the three, it is permissible; and if he delivered the khutbah in the presence of [women] alone? It is permissible. In Fath al-Qadir: the relied-upon [position] is that if he delivered the khutbah alone, he does so, taking [from] their statement that it is conditioned in his presence. Regarding the tasbihah and tahmidah, it is said [they must be] with the intention of the khutbah; if he praised [Allah] for sneezing, it does not suffice for the obligatory [part]. It contains an apparent objection because it does not indicate what he mentioned by any type of indication, as is not hidden. And it is corrected in al-Zahiriyyah that if he delivered the khutbah alone, it is not permissible. In al-Mudmarat, attributed to al-Zad: Does the khutbah take the place of the two rak'ahs? The mashayikh differed: some said it does, and therefore it is only permissible after the entry of time; some said it does not, which is the more correct, because all conditions are not required for it such as facing the qiblah, purity, etc. In al-Bada'i: Then it, although it takes the place of the two rak'ahs, is a condition and not a pillar, because Friday prayer is not established by the khutbah, so it is not from its pillars. In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the khutbah is a condition for the inception (in'iqad) with respect to the one who initiates the tahrimah for Friday, not with respect to everyone who prays it. The condition of presence of one or a group is to realize the meaning of the khutbah, because it is from relative matters. Hence they said: If the imam becomes impure and someone who did not witness the khutbah is brought forward, it is permissible for him to lead them in Friday prayer, because his tahrimah is based on that initiated tahrimah. So the khutbah is a condition for the inception of Friday prayers only with respect to the one who initiates the tahrimah. Do you not see its validity for followers who did not witness the khutbah? On this basis, the analogical reasoning would be that if this successor invalidated [his prayer], it would not be permissible for him to lead them in Friday prayer again, but they preferred by istihsan the permissibility of his leading them again because when he took the place of the first, he is annexed to him in ruling. So if the first became invalid, the second may lead. If the first became impure before starting, and someone who did not witness the khutbah is brought forward, it is not permissible. The author did not condition that he prays immediately after the khutbah without delay, indicating that it is not a condition. Therefore they said: The khutbah is repeated as a matter of priority if the imam remembers a missed prayer during Friday prayer, even if it was witr, such that it becomes invalid? For them, likewise the first? And whether the appointment of another is correct is subject to contemplation, and it has parallels in the book of waqf. Comment in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And consider what is the cause of contemplation, for the mosque by its demolition does not lose its mosque status unlike the city. Look at Fatawa Ibn al-Shilbi. His statement: 'And it has an apparent objection...' said al-Ramli from Shaykh al-Maqdisi: This is not the text of Fath al-Qadir, rather you turned it and presented and delayed to be able to bring what you chose. The text of the muhaqqiq after mentioning the Imam's statement regarding the sufficiency of 'al-hamdu lillah' and similar in the khutbah, and that it is called 'khutbah' linguistically even if not customarily, and that custom is considered only in people's mutual dealings for indicating their purpose, but in matters between a servant and his Lord, the literal meaning of the word is considered. Then he said: This speech is the relied-upon for Abu Hanifah, so it becomes necessary to consider what derives from it, meaning the narration of not requiring attendance. His brother also objected to it in al-Nahr, but the muhaqqiq discussed after quoting his speech, and the summary is that the evidence only indicates that the condition is absolute dhikr called 'khutbah' linguistically, not restricted by the presence of [people]. Therefore Friday prayer is occupied with performing it. Likewise, if he invalidated Friday prayer and needed to repeat it, or he began a supererogatory prayer after the khutbah and did not repeat the khutbah, it suffices him. Likewise if he delivered the khutbah while junub. So in Fath al-Qadir. He did not distinguish between a short and long interval, but distinguished between them in al-Khulasah: If he delivered the khutbah while impure or junub, then performed wudu or ghusl and prayed, it is permissible. If he delivered the khutbah then returned to his home, had lunch or had intercourse and performed ghusl, then came, he repeats the khutbah. So also in al-Muhit, with the rationale that the first is from the acts of prayer unlike the second. The apparent meaning is that repeating is necessary in the second, otherwise there is no difference between all [cases]. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, he explicitly stated the necessity of restarting and the invalidity of the khutbah, and this is the apparent because if the interval becomes long, it is no longer a khutbah for Friday, unlike when it is short. It is known from their furu' that it is not required for the imam to be the khatib. And al-Khulasah explicitly stated that if a minor delivered the khutbah with the permission of the sultan, and an adult man led the Friday prayer, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of presence (hudur) for the validity of the Friday khutbah, and related subsidiary issues. The discussion begins by noting that the apparent ruling from the matn is that the presence of a single person does not suffice for the khutbah to be valid. However, al-Khulasah contradicts this, stating that if the khatib delivers the khutbah alone with no one present, it is not permissible. In al-Asl, there are two narrations: one requiring at least one, another allowing it. The passage then presents the relied-upon position from Fath al-Qadir that delivering the khutbah alone is permissible, based on the principle that the khutbah is valid with the mere utterance of dhikr intended as khutbah. This is supported by the linguistic meaning of the term. The commentator notes an apparent objection to this, but the text clarifies that the dalil (evidence) shows that the condition is absolute dhikr, not tied to a crowd. The issue of whether the khutbah stands in place of the two rak'ahs is then discussed: some say it does, hence it requires time; others say it does not, which is the more correct view, because conditions like qiblah and purity are not required for the khutbah. The passage then explains that the khutbah is a condition for the inception (in'iqad) of Friday prayer only for the one who initiates the tahrimah, not for the followers. This is why if the imam becomes impure, a person who did not hear the khutbah can lead the prayer. Various furu' (branches) are discussed: the imam's hadath, the interval between khutbah and prayer, the permissibility of a minor as khatib, and the condition that the imam need not be the khatib. Throughout, the text presents different Hanafi authorities (Fath al-Qadir, al-Khulasah, al-Zahiriyyah, etc.) and their positions, with the mufta bihi being that one person suffices and that the khutbah can be given alone.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered before Friday prayer, consisting of dhikr and admonition, which is a condition (shart) for the validity of Friday prayer in the Hanafi school.
شرط الانعقاد (shart al-in'iqaad): A condition for the inception of the validity of an act; here, the khutbah is a condition for the validity of the Friday prayer only for the one who initiates the tahrimah.
الحضور (al-hudur): The presence of an audience for the khutbah; a disputed condition within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is invalid if less than 40 people are present.

C) It requires at least three listeners.
D) It must be delivered by a minor with adult supervision.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah in the Hanafi school is valid with a single listener; the essential element is the intention and utterance of dhikr, not a crowd.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Sunnah and obligatory components of the Friday khutbah
Listing the fard and sunnah of the Friday khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two obligatory (fard) components of the Friday khutbah and list its fifteen sunnah (recommended) components according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah has only two obligatory elements: time and dhikr; all else is sunnah.

The Friday khutbah is a condition for Friday prayer, not a pillar. Many assume it has many obligatory parts, but the Hanafi school limits the fard to just two: the time and the remembrance of Allah. This lesson clarifies the essential versus recommended components as listed in the classical texts, helping you distinguish what is necessary from what is praiseworthy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two fard (obligatory) components
Read the passage and note that only time (al-waqt) and remembrance of Allah (dhikr Allah) are considered fard. Everything else is sunnah.
This is the core of the lesson.
2
Distinguish fard from sunnah in the khutbah
Understand that omitting a fard invalidates the khutbah; omitting a sunnah makes it valid but disliked (makruh).
This distinction is crucial for proper practice.
3
Memorize the fifteen sunan (recommended acts)
Use the passage to memorize the list: purity (taharah), standing, facing the congregation, seeking refuge internally, ensuring the people hear (even if they don't), delivering a light khutbah (which includes ten sub-items: beginning with hamd, extolling Allah, the two shahadahs, sending blessings on the Prophet, admonition, recitation of Quran, etc.), two khutbahs with a sitting between them, supplication for believers in the second khutbah, and making the intention for the khutbah. Note that Abu Yusuf differs on purity, requiring it for validity.
Use mnemonic techniques to remember the fifteen.
4
Understand the preferred practice (khutbah khafifah)
The passage recommends a brief khutbah as per Abu Hanifah. Recognize that brevity is a sunnah, not a requirement.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on conciseness.
5
Note the intra-madhhab difference on purity
While the text says purity is sunnah and it is makruh to deliver without it, Abu Yusuf holds it is not permissible (la yajuz). Understand the difference in rulings.
This is a minor ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

قوله ( وسن خطبتان بجلسة بينهما وطهارة قائماً كما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال : ينبغي أن يخطب خطبة خفيفة يفتتح بحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويتشهد ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويعظ ويذكر ويقرأ سورة ثم يجلس جلسة خفيفة، ثم يقوم فيخطب خطبة أخرى يحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويتشهد ويصلي على النبي و هو يدعو للمؤمنين والمؤمنات كما في البدائع . وقد علم من هذا أنه لا يعظ في الثانية ولهذا قال في التجنيس : إن الثانية كالأولى إلا أنه يدعو للمسلمين مكان الوعظ وظاهره أنه يسن قراءة آية في الثانية كالأولى.. والحاصل كما في المجتبي أن الكلام في الخطبة في أربعة مواضع: في الخطبة والخطيب والمستمع وشهود الخطبة. أما الخطبة فتشتمل على فرض وسنة فأما الفرض فشيئين : الوقت وذكر الله تعالى، وأما سننها فخمس عشرة : أحدها الطهارة حتى كرهت للمحدث والجنب. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يجوز . وثانيها القيام. وثالثها استقبال القوم بوجهه ورابعها قال أبو يوسف في الجوامع : التعوذ في نفسه قبل الخطبة وخامسها أن . يسمع القوم الخطبة فإن لم يسمع أجزأه . وسادسها ما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يخطب خطبة خفيفة وهي تشتمل على عشرة : أحدها البداءة بحمد الله . وثانيها الثناء عليه بماهو أهله وثالثها الشهادتان . ورابعها الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وخامسها العظة والتذكير وسادسها قراءة القرآن وتاركها مسيء وروي أنه قرأ فيها سورة العصر ومرة أخرى لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة
His statement: 'And it is sunnah: two khutbahs with a sitting between them, purity, standing.' As narrated from Abu Hanifah that he said: He should deliver a light khutbah, opening with praise of Allah, extolling Him, reciting the shahadah, sending blessings on the Prophet, admonishing and reminding, reciting a surah, then sit briefly, then stand and deliver another khutbah in which he praises Allah, extols Him, recites the shahadah, sends blessings on the Prophet, and supplicates for believing men and women, as in al-Bada'i. It is known from this that he does not admonish in the second; hence al-Tajnis said: The second is like the first except that he supplicates for the Muslims in place of admonition. And its apparent meaning is that reciting a verse in the second is sunnah like the first. The summary, as in al-Mujtaba, is that the discussion about the khutbah covers four areas: the khutbah, the khatib, the listener, and the witnessing of the khutbah. As for the khutbah, it comprises fard and sunnah. The fard are two things: time and the remembrance of Allah. Its sunan are fifteen: first, purity (taharah), to the extent that it is disliked for the person with minor or major impurity. Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible. Second, standing. Third, facing the people with his face. Fourth, as Abu Yusuf said in al-Jawami': seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) internally before the khutbah. Fifth, that the people hear the khutbah; if they do not hear, it suffices. Sixth, what Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifah that he delivers a light khutbah, which comprises ten things: first, beginning with praise of Allah; second, extolling Him as He deserves; third, the two shahadahs; fourth, sending blessings on the Prophet; fifth, admonition and reminder; sixth, recitation of the Quran. The one who omits it is sinful. It is narrated that he recited Surah al-Asr, and another time 'Not equal are the inhabitants of the Fire and the inhabitants of Paradise'.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the sunnah and obligatory (fard) components of the Friday khutbah. It begins by establishing that two khutbahs with a sitting between them are sunnah, along with the khatib being in a state of purity and standing. The content of each khutbah is described: the first includes praise, shahadah, salawat, admonition, and recitation of a surah; the second includes praise, shahadah, salawat, and supplication for believers, but no admonition. The discussion then categorizes the khutbah into four aspects: the khutbah itself, the khatib, the listener, and the witnessing. For the khutbah, the fard (obligatory) elements are only two: the time (i.e., it must be delivered within the time of Friday prayer) and the remembrance of Allah (dhikr). The sunan are fifteen, as enumerated: 1) purity (taharah) — it is makruh to deliver the khutbah while impure; Abu Yusuf holds it is impermissible. 2) standing. 3) facing the people. 4) seeking refuge internally before starting. 5) ensuring the people hear the khutbah (but if they do not hear, it still suffices). 6-15) From the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifah, the khutbah should be light and include ten items: beginning with hamd, extolling Allah, the two shahadahs, salawat, admonition, recitation of Quran (the one who omits it is sinful — indicating it is wajib or at least sunnah muakkadah). The passage closes with examples of what the Prophet recited in the khutbah. This enumeration serves as a concise reference for the obligations and recommended practices of the Friday sermon.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory element of the khutbah; here only two: time and dhikr of Allah.
سنة (sunnah): Recommended actions in the khutbah; omitting them does not invalidate the khutbah but is blameworthy.
خطبة خفيفة (khutbah khafifah): A light or brief khutbah, recommended by Abu Hanifah, containing the essential components without lengthy speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is considered a fard (obligatory) in the Friday khutbah?
A) Purification (taharah) of the khatib.
B) Standing during the khutbah.
C) The time of the khutbah and the remembrance of Allah.
D) Recitation of a Quranic verse.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah has only two obligatory elements: time and dhikr; the remaining fifteen items are sunnah, whose omission does not invalidate the khutbah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Fard and Sunnah of the Friday Khutbah with the Dispute on Purity
Expansion on conditions and sunan of the Friday khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the fard (obligatory) and sunnah (recommended) elements of the Friday khutbah and state the Hanafi ruling on impurity of the khatib, evaluating the intra-Hanafi objection of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The khutbah's only fard are time and dhikr; purity is sunnah, and omitting it does not invalidate.

The Friday khutbah is a distinct act with its own structure. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the matn's statement that two khutbahs, purity, and standing are sunnah. It then enumerates the obligatory and recommended components and dives into the dispute over whether the khatib must be pure. The key is understanding which elements are binding and which are merely recommended, as this affects the validity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fard (obligatory) of the khutbah
From the commentary, extract the two essential elements that must be present for the khutbah to be valid: the time (after zawal) and the remembrance of Allah (dhikr).
These are the only fard; everything else is sunnah or condition.
2
List the fifteen sunan of the khutbah
The passage enumerates fifteen recommended practices. Group them into those related to the khatib's state (purity, standing, facing the people), the content (praise, testimony, blessings, exhortation, Quran recitation), and the delivery (two parts with sitting, audibility, shortness).
The sunan are drawn from the Prophet's consistent practice.
3
Analyse the dispute on purity (taharah)
Identify the positions of Abu Hanifa (sunnah, makruh if omitted) and Abu Yusuf (la yajuz, i.e. not permissible). Understand the underlying reasoning: Abu Yusuf analogizes the khutbah to prayer, while Abu Hanifa sees it as a condition, not prayer itself.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequence: the khutbah's validity.
4
Determine the effect of a long interruption
The passage differentiates between short and long breaks between the khutbah and prayer. A long break (e.g., going home for lunch) necessitates a new khutbah. This is linked to the nature of the khutbah as an act of prayer connected to the Salat al-Jumu'ah.
The ruling is based on the principle that a long interval breaks the continuity.
5
Apply the distinction between fard and sunnah to a scenario
Consider a khatib who gives the khutbah without praising Allah (only dhikr) while impure. Identify which elements are missing and whether the khutbah is valid. Use the hierarchy: fard (dhikr present) → valid but makruh for missing sunan (purity and praise).
This reinforces the operational difference between obligatory and recommended.

كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة الجمعة
الظهر فتبطل بخروجه والخطبة قبلها وسن خطبتان بجلسة بينهما وطهارة قائماً وكفت
الجمعة لذلك فاشتغل بقضائها، وكذا لو كان أفسد الجمعة فاحتاج إلى إعادتها أو افتتح التطوع بعد الخطبة وإن لم يعد الخطبة ، أجزأه وكذا إذا خطب جنباً. كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يفرق بين الفصل القليل والكثير ، وفرق بينهما في الخلاصة فقال : ولو خطب محدثاً أو جنباً ثم توضأ أو اغتسل وصلى جاز، ولو خطب ثم رجع إلى بيته فتغدى أو جامع واغتسل ثم جاء استقبل الخطبة، وكذا في المحيط معللاً بأن الأول من أعمال الصلاة بخلاف الثاني فإن ظاهره أن الاستقبال في الثاني لازم وإلا فلا فرق بين الكل. وقد صرح في السراج الوهاج بلزوم الاستئناف وبطلان الخطبة وهذا هو الظاهر لأنه إذا طال الفصل لم يبق خطبة للجمعة بخلاف ما إذا قل، وقد علم من تفاريعهم أنه لا يشترط في الإمام أن يكون هو الخطيب، وقد صرح الخلاصة بأنه لو خطب صبي بإذن السلطان وصلى الجمعة رجل بالغ يجوز .
قوله (وسن خطبتان بجلسة بينهما وطهارة (قائماً كما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال : ينبغي أن يخطب خطبة خفيفة يفتتح بحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويتشهد ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويعظ ويذكر ويقرأ سورة ثم يجلس جلسة خفيفة، ثم يقوم فيخطب خطبة أخرى يحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويتشهد ويصلي على النبي و هو يدعو للمؤمنين والمؤمنات كما في البدائع . وقد علم من هذا أنه لا يعظ في الثانية ولهذا قال في التجنيس : إن الثانية كالأولى إلا أنه يدعو للمسلمين مكان الوعظ وظاهره أنه يسن قراءة آية في الثانية كالأولى.. والحاصل كما في المجتبي أن الكلام في الخطبة في أربعة مواضع: في الخطبة والخطيب والمستمع وشهود الخطبة. أما الخطبة فتشتمل على فرض وسنة فأما الفرض فشيئان : الوقت وذكر الله تعالى، وأما سننها فخمس عشرة : أحدها الطهارة حتى كرهت للمحدث والجنب. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يجوز . وثانيها القيام. وثالثها استقبال القوم بوجهه ورابعها قال أبو يوسف في الجوامع : التعوذ في نفسه قبل الخطبة وخامسها أن . يسمع القوم الخطبة فإن لم يسمع أجزأه . وسادسها ما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يخطب خطبة خفيفة وهي تشتمل على عشرة : أحدها البداءة بحمد الله . وثانيها الثناء عليه بماهو أهله وثالثها الشهادتان . ورابعها الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وخامسها العظة والتذكير وسادسها قراءة القرآن وتاركها مسيء وروي أنه قرأ فيها سورة العصر ومرة أخرى لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة
أحد فيعتبر فيه حقيقة اللفظ، وهذا ظاهر في اقتضائه صحتها وحده لأن اشتراط قصد التحميدة ونحوها يقتضي أنه لو خطب وحده جاز لكن لقائل أن يقول إن الأمر بالسعي إلى الذكر ليس إلا لاستماعه والمأمور جمع فإذا جازت وحده لم يجز الأمر فائدته وكأن هذا هو وجه ما رجحه في به الشارح من اشتراط حضرة جماعة تنعقد الجمعة على ما مر . بهم
جزم
ما الظهيرية، وبه يترجح قوله : ( وقد صرح في الخلاصة بأنه لو خطب صبي الخ) قال في الظهيرية : لو خطب صبي
أصحاب الجنة هم الفائزون﴾ [الحشر: ٢٠] وأخرى ونادوا يا مالك﴾ [الزخرف: ٧٧] وسابعها الجلوس بين الخطبتين. وثامنها أن يعيد في الخطبة الثانية الحمد لله والثناء والصلاة على النبي . تاسعها أن يزيد فيها الدعاء للمؤمنين والمؤمنات وعاشرها تخفيف الخطبتين بقدر سورة من طوال المفصل ويكره التطويل، وأما الخطيب فيشترط فيه أن يتأهل للإمامة في الجمعة والسنة في حقه الطهارة والقيام والاستقبال بوجهه للقوم وترك السلام من خروجه إلى دخوله في الصلاة وترك الكلام. وقال الشافعي : إذا استوى على المنبر سلم على القوم، وقوله لا إذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام يبطل ذلك . وأما المستمع فيستقبل الإمام إذا بدأ بالخطبة وينصت ولا يتكلم ولا يرد السلام ولا يشمت ولا يصلي على النبي . وقالا : يصلي السامع في نفسه، وفي جواز قراءة القرآن وذكر الفقه والنظر فيه لمن يستمع الخطبة اختلاف المشايخ. ويكره لمستمع الخطبة ما يكره في الصلاة كالأكل والشرب والعبث والالتفات، وأما التخطي فمكروه عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : إنما يكره بعد خروج الإمام. وقال الرازي : إنما يجوز قبله إذا لم يؤذ أحداً فأما تخطي السؤال فمكروه في جميع الأحوال بالإجماع وأما شهود الخطبة فشرط في حق الإمام دون المأموم .اهـ. ما في المجتبي .
هو
وأطلق المصنف في الجلسة ولم يبين قدرها للاختلاف ؛ فعند الطحاوي مقدار ما يمس موضع جلوسه من المنبر، وفي ظاهر الرواية مقدار ثلاث آيات كما في التجنيس وغيره، ومن الغريب ما ذكره في السراج الوهاج أنه يستحب للإمام إذا صعد المنبر وأقبل على الناس أن يسلم عليهم لأنه استدبرهم في صعوده .اهـ. ومن المستحب أن يرفع الخطيب صوته كما في السراج الوهاج ومنه أن يكون الجهر في الثانية دون الأولى كما في شرح الطحاوي وفي التجنيس : وينبغي أن تكون الخطبة الثانية الحمد لله نحمده ونستعينه إلى آخره . لأن هذا الثانية التي كان يخطب بها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكر الخلفاء الراشدين مستحسن، بذلك جرى التوارث ويذكر العمين .اهـ. ثم قولهم إن السنة في المستمع استقبال الإمام مخالف لما عليه عمل الناس من استقبال المستمع للقبلة ولهذا قال في التجنيس والرسم في زماننا أن القوم يستقبلون القبلة قال : لأنهم لو استقبلوا الإمام الخرجوا في تسوية الصفوف بعد فراغه لكثرة الزحام. وجزم في الخلاصة بأنه يستحب استقباله إن كان أمام الإمام، فإن كان عن يمين الإمام أو عن يساره قريباً من الإمام ينحرف إلى الإمام مستعداً للسماع. ومن السنة أن يكون الخطيب على منبر اقتداء برسول الله . وفي المضمرات معزياً إلى روضة العلماء : الحكمة أن الخطيب يتقلد سيفاً ما قد سمعت الفقيه أبا الحسن الرستغفني يقول : كل بلدة فتحت عنوة بالسيف يخطب الخطيب على منبرها متقلداً بالسيف يريهم أنها فتحت بالسيف فإذا رجعتم عن الإسلام فذلك السيف باقٍ في أيدي المسلمين نقاتلكم به حتى ترجعوا إلى الإسلام، وكل بلدة أسلم أهلها طوعاً يخطبون فيها بلا سيف ومدينة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فتحت بالقرآن فيخطب
The book of prayer, chapter on Friday prayer. ... So he becomes occupied with making it up. Similarly, if he spoiled the Friday prayer and needed to repeat it, or he began a voluntary prayer after the sermon without repeating the sermon, it suffices him, and also if he gave the sermon while in a state of major impurity. Likewise in Fath al-Qadir. And he did not differentiate between a short and long interval, but in al-Khulasa he differentiated: If he gave the sermon while in a state of minor or major impurity, then performed wudu or ghusl and prayed, it is permissible. If he gave the sermon then returned home, had lunch or intercourse, then performed ghusl and came back, he must restart the sermon. Similarly in al-Muhit, explaining that the former is from the acts of prayer while the latter is not, so it is apparent that restarting is necessary in the latter; otherwise there is no difference between all cases. It is explicitly stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that restarting is necessary and the sermon is invalid, and this is evidently correct because if the interval is long, it is no longer a Friday sermon, unlike when it is short. It is known from their derived rulings that the imam need not be the khatib. Al-Khulasa explicitly states that if a minor gave the sermon with the sultan's permission and an adult man led the Friday prayer, it is permissible. His statement: 'It is sunnah to have two sermons with a sitting between them, purity, standing' as narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: He should give a light sermon, beginning with praise of Allah, extolling Him, reciting the testimony, sending blessings on the Prophet, exhorting, reminding, reciting a sura, then sit briefly, then stand and give another sermon praising Allah, extolling Him, reciting the testimony, sending blessings on the Prophet, and he supplicates for believing men and women, as in al-Bada'i. It is understood from this that he does not exhort in the second, hence in al-Tajnisa it is said: The second is like the first except he supplicates for the Muslims in place of exhortation. It is apparent that it is sunnah to recite a verse in the second as in the first. The gist, as in al-Mujtaba, is that the discussion about the sermon covers four topics: the sermon, the khatib, the listener, and attending the sermon. As for the sermon, it comprises obligatory and sunnah elements. The obligatory elements are two: the time and the remembrance of Allah. The sunan are fifteen: first, purity, to the extent that it is disliked for one in minor or major impurity. Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible. Second, standing. Third, facing the people with his face. Fourth, as Abu Yusuf said in al-Jawami': seeking refuge in himself before the sermon. Fifth, that the people hear the sermon; if they do not hear, it suffices. Sixth, what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: that he gives a light sermon, which comprises ten things: first, beginning with praise of Allah; second, extolling Him as is befitting; third, the two testimonies; fourth, sending blessings on the Prophet; fifth, exhortation and reminding; sixth, recitation of Quran; and he who omits it is doing wrong. It is narrated that he recited therein Surat al-Asr and another time: 'Not equal are the companions of the Fire and the companions of Paradise.' ... One, so the literal meaning is considered in it. This is apparent in requiring its validity alone, because requiring the intention of the 'all praise' and similar implies that if he gave the sermon alone, it would be permissible. But someone may say that the command to hasten to the remembrance is only for its listening, and those commanded are a group. So if it were permissible alone, the benefit of the command would not occur. And it seems this is the reasoning for what the commentator preferred regarding the condition of the presence of a congregation by which Friday prayer is valid, as previously mentioned. ... It is decided in al-Zahiriyya, and by it his statement is strengthened: 'And he explicitly stated in al-Khulasa that if a minor gave the sermon...' He said in al-Zahiriyya: If a minor gave the sermon... 'The companions of Paradise are the successful' [59:20] and another: 'And they call out, O Malik!' [43:77] Seventh, the sitting between the two sermons. Eighth, that he repeats in the second sermon praise of Allah, extolling, and sending blessings on the Prophet. Ninth, that he adds supplication for believing men and women. Tenth, shortening the two sermons to the length of a sura from the long mufassal, and prolonging is disliked. As for the khatib: it is required that he be qualified for leading the Friday prayer. The sunnah for him is purity, standing, facing the people with his face, refraining from greeting from his departure until entering the prayer, and refraining from speech. Al-Shafi'i said: When he ascends the pulpit, he greets the people. His statement: 'No, when the imam comes out, there is no prayer nor speech, that invalidates it.' As for the listener: he faces the imam when he begins the sermon, listens attentively, does not speak, does not return greetings, does not say 'Yarhamukallah' to a sneezer, and does not send blessings on the Prophet. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The listener may send blessings in his heart. There is difference of opinion among the shuyukh regarding the permissibility of reciting Quran, studying fiqh, and reflecting for one who listens to the sermon. It is disliked for the listener of the sermon what is disliked in prayer, such as eating, drinking, fidgeting, and turning away. As for stepping over people, it is disliked according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is only disliked after the imam comes out. Al-Razi said: It is only permissible before if he does not harm anyone. As for stepping over the questioner, it is disliked in all cases by consensus. As for attending the sermon, it is a condition for the imam, not for the follower. End of what is in al-Mujtaba. And the author left the length of the sitting unspecified due to difference; according to al-Tahawi, it is the amount to touch his sitting place on the pulpit. In the apparent narration, it is the amount of three verses, as in al-Tajnisa and others. Strange is what was mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that it is recommended for the imam when he ascends the pulpit and faces the people to greet them, because he turned his back to them during his ascent. End. Among the recommended things is that the khatib raise his voice, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and that the loudness in the second be less than the first, as in Sharh al-Tahawi. In al-Tajnisa: The second sermon should be: 'All praise is due to Allah, we praise Him and seek His help' etc., because this is the second sermon that the Messenger of Allah used to deliver, and mentioning the rightly-guided caliphs is commendable; upon that practice has been inherited, and he mentions the two uncles. End. Then their statement that the sunnah for the listener is to face the imam contradicts what people do, which is facing the qibla. Hence, in al-Tajnisa it is said: The practice in our time is that the people face the qibla. He said: Because if they faced the imam, they would be disordered in straightening the rows after he finishes due to the great crowding. In al-Khulasa, it is decided that it is recommended to face him if one is in front of the imam. If one is to the right or left of the imam, close to him, he turns toward the imam ready to listen. And it is sunnah for the khatib to be on a minbar, following the example of the Messenger of Allah. In al-Mudmarat, attributed to Rawdat al-Ulama: The wisdom is that the khatib carries a sword. I have heard the faqih Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani say: Every town conquered by force of the sword, the khatib gives the sermon on its minbar carrying a sword to show that it was conquered by the sword; if you turn away from Islam, that sword remains in the hands of Muslims to fight you with until you return to Islam. Every town whose people accepted Islam voluntarily, they give the sermon without a sword. The city of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was conquered by the Quran, so he gives the sermon...
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the rulings and sunan of the Friday khutbah. It begins by discussing scenarios where the khutbah might be interrupted or the khatib is impure, noting a difference between short and long interruptions: a long break invalidates the khutbah, while a short break does not. It then explains the statement of the matn that the khutbah consists of two sermons with a sitting between, and that purity and standing are sunnah. The commentary provides a detailed list of obligatory elements (time and dhikr of Allah) and fifteen sunan, including purity, standing, facing the people, seeking refuge, audibility, and the content of the sermon (praise, testimony, blessings, exhortation, Quran recitation). It also covers the conditions for the khatib (being qualified for imamah, with recommended acts) and for the listener (facing the imam, silence, refraining from worldly actions). A notable ikhtilaf is mentioned: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh for an impure person to give the khutbah, while Abu Yusuf holds it invalid. The passage also cites al-Shafi'i's view that the imam should greet the congregation on the pulpit. Practical considerations are given, such as the recommended length of the sitting between sermons (three verses in the apparent riwaya) and the modern practice of listeners facing the qibla rather than the imam due to crowding. The wisdom of the khatib carrying a sword is explained based on the nature of the conquest of the town.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday prayer, consisting of two parts with a sitting in between.
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice; omission is disliked but not sinful or invalidating.
فرض (fard): Obligatory element; omission invalidates the act. Here, the fard of the khutbah are time and dhikr.
محدث (muhdith): One in a state of minor ritual impurity (without wudu).
جنب (junub): One in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many sunan (recommended acts) are listed for the Friday khutbah?
A) 10
B) 12
C) 15
D) 20

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah has only two obligatory elements (time and dhikr); all other requirements are sunnah, and missing them does not invalidate the prayer, though it is makruh.

Recommended Acts of the Friday Khutbah (7-10) and Related Sunnahs
Lists the last four recommended acts and discusses sitting duration and second khutbah content.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four recommended acts of the Friday khutbah (7-10), explain the Hanafi position on the duration of sitting between the khutbahs, and identify the recommended content of the second khutbah.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah has ten recommended acts; sitting between them is a sunnah (not a pillar) and the authoritative duration is three verses.

The previous lesson covered the first six recommended acts of the Friday khutbah. This lesson completes the list with items seven through ten, and then discusses the sitting between the two khutbahs and the content of the second khutbah. Understanding these details helps the khatib perform the khutbah in the best manner according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Four Recommended Acts (7-10)
Read the text carefully and write down the four recommended acts mentioned as seventh, eighth, ninth, and tenth. Note the specific wording for each.
These are additions to the first six acts covered earlier.
2
Analyze the Duration of the Sitting
Identify the two opinions: al-Tahawi's view (time to rest on the minbar) and the zahir al-riwaya view (three verses). Determine which is mufta bihi and why.
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq left it unrestricted due to disagreement.
3
Examine the Additional Recommendations
Look at the recommendations about greeting upon ascending the minbar, raising the voice, lowering volume in the second khutbah, and the phrasing of the second khutbah (al-hamdu lillah nahmaduhu...). Also note the mention of the caliphs and uncles.
Some of these are from other sources (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, Sharh al-Tahawi, al-Tajnīs).
4
Recognize the Ruling on Prolongation
The text states that prolonging the khutbah is makruh tanzihi (disliked). Understand that brevity is recommended, with the khutbahs kept to about a surah from the long mufassal.
This applies to both khutbahs together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسابعها الجلوس بين الخطبتين. وثامنها أن يعيد في الخطبة الثانية الحمد لله والثناء والصلاة على النبي . تاسعها أن يزيد فيها الدعاء للمؤمنين والمؤمنات وعاشرها تخفيف الخطبتين بقدر سورة من طوال المفصل ويكره التطويل، وأطلق المصنف في الجلسة ولم يبين قدرها للاختلاف ؛ فعند الطحاوي مقدار ما يمس موضع جلوسه من المنبر، وفي ظاهر الرواية مقدار ثلاث آيات كما في التجنيس وغيره، ومن الغريب ما ذكره في السراج الوهاج أنه يستحب للإمام إذا صعد المنبر وأقبل على الناس أن يسلم عليهم لأنه استدبرهم في صعوده .اهـ. ومن المستحب أن يرفع الخطيب صوته كما في السراج الوهاج ومنه أن يكون الجهر في الثانية دون الأولى كما في شرح الطحاوي وفي التجنيس : وينبغي أن تكون الخطبة الثانية الحمد لله نحمده ونستعينه إلى آخره . لأن هذا الثانية التي كان يخطب بها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكر الخلفاء الراشدين مستحسن، بذلك جرى التوارث ويذكر العمين .اهـ.
And the seventh is sitting between the two khutbahs. And the eighth is that he repeats in the second khutbah praise of Allah, extolment, and salutation upon the Prophet. The ninth is that he adds in it supplication for believing men and women. The tenth is shortening the two khutbahs to the extent of a surah from the long mufassal, and prolongation is disliked. The author [of Kanz al-Daqa'iq] gave an unrestricted statement about the sitting and did not specify its extent due to disagreement. According to al-Tahawi, it is the amount that touches his sitting place on the minbar. In the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), it is the amount of three verses as in al-Tajnīs and others. It is strange what was mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that it is recommended for the imam, when he ascends the minbar and faces the people, to greet them, because he turned his back to them while ascending. From the recommended [acts] is that the khatib raise his voice. And from them is that the loudness in the second [khutbah] be less than in the first, as in Sharh al-Tahawi. In al-Tajnīs: The second khutbah should be 'al-ḥamdu lillāh naḥmaduhu wa nastaʿīnuh...' because this is the second khutbah with which the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to deliver, and mentioning the Rightly Guided Caliphs is commendable; this is how transmission has proceeded, and he mentions both uncles.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing the last four recommended acts of the Friday khutbah, and then discusses the sitting between the two khutbahs, its duration, and the recommended content of the second khutbah. The author, Zayla'i, notes that Imam Muhammad al-Tahawi held the sitting to be the time it takes one to rest on the minbar, whereas the zahir al-riwaya (from Imam Muhammad's six books) specifies it as the duration of reciting three verses. The text also recounts an unusual view from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj recommending the imam to greet the congregation upon ascending the minbar, contrary to the earlier ruling that he should not greet. It then recommends that the khatib raise his voice and that the second khutbah be quieter than the first. The wording of the second khutbah should include 'al-hamdu lillah nahmaduhu wa nasta'inuh'—the same form the Prophet ﷺ used—and it is commendable to mention the four caliphs and the Prophet's uncles (Hamza and al-‘Abbas).

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered on Friday before the congregational prayer, comprising two parts with a sitting in between.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The authoritative transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
الجلوس بين الخطبتين (al-julūs bayn al-khuṭbatayn): The sitting between the two parts of the Friday sermon, which is a sunnah act.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah includes ten sunnah acts; the sitting between the two parts is a sunnah (not a pillar) and its authoritative duration is three verses.
