Conditions and Sunnahs of the Friday Khatib
Lists qualifications and sunnahs of the Friday khatib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition and sunnah acts for the Friday khatib, explain the Hanafi position on greeting and the sword tradition, and identify the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The khatib must be fit to lead; his sunnah includes purity, standing, and refraining from speech and greeting.

This lesson examines the qualifications and recommended practices of the Friday khatib according to the Hanafi school. We will explore the necessary condition of being qualified for imamah, the sunnah acts of the khatib upon the minbar, and two notable issues: the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over greeting the congregation, and the tradition of carrying a sword. The passage also addresses the practice of supplicating for the ruler, which is deemed an innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for the khatib
The text states: 'يشترط فيه أن يتأهل للإمامة في الجمعة' – the khatib must be qualified to lead the Jumu'ah prayer. This is a necessary condition (shart) for the validity of his khutbah.
Qualification includes being Muslim, male, sane, adult, and knowledgeable in the rulings of Jumu'ah.
2
List the sunnah acts of the khatib
The passage lists: purity (طهارة), standing (قيام), facing the people (استقبال بوجهه للقوم), refraining from greeting from exit to entering prayer (ترك السلام), refraining from speech (ترك الكلام), and delivering from a minbar (منبر). These are recommended practices.
These sunnah acts are not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the khutbah.
3
Analyze the greeting dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the khatib should greet the congregation upon ascending the minbar. The Hanafi position is that he should not, because after the imam steps out, speech is prohibited (لا صلاة ولا كلام). The greeting would constitute speech and thus is not allowed.
The thamarah (practical difference): Hanafis do not greet, Shafi'is do.
4
Understand the sword tradition
In cities conquered by force, it is sunnah for the khatib to be girded with a sword (متقلداً بالسيف) as a symbol of strength. He does not hold it in his hand. Leaning on a bow or stick is disliked, but the sword is an exception.
The tradition traces back to al-Mudmarat and is specific to conquered cities; in cities surrendered peacefully, no sword is used.
5
Evaluate supplication for the ruler
The passage states that supplication for the ruler (الدعاء للسلطان) in the khutbah is not recommended, as it is an innovation (محدث). The original khutbah was only for reminder.
This reflects an early Hanafi view; some later scholars allowed it for public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الخطيب فيشترط فيه أن يتأهل للإمامة في الجمعة والسنة في حقه الطهارة والقيام والاستقبال بوجهه للقوم وترك السلام من خروجه إلى دخوله في الصلاة وترك الكلام. وقال الشافعي : إذا استوى على المنبر سلم على القوم، وقوله لا إذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام يبطل ذلك . ومن السنة أن يكون الخطيب على منبر اقتداء برسول الله . وفي المضمرات معزياً إلى روضة العلماء : الحكمة أن الخطيب يتقلد سيفاً ما قد سمعت الفقيه أبا الحسن الرستغفني يقول : كل بلدة فتحت عنوة بالسيف يخطب الخطيب على منبرها متقلداً بالسيف يريهم أنها فتحت بالسيف فإذا رجعتم عن الإسلام فذلك السيف باقٍ في أيدي المسلمين نقاتلكم به حتى ترجعوا إلى الإسلام، وكل بلدة أسلم أهلها طوعاً يخطبون فيها بلا سيف ومدينة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فتحت بالقرآن فيخطب الخطيب بلا سيف وتكون تلك البلدة عشرية ومكة فتحت بالسيف فيخطب مع السيف اهـ . وهذا مفيد لكونه يتقلد بالسيف لا أنه يمسكه بيده كما هو المتعارف مع أن ظاهر ما في الخلاصة كراهة ذلك فإنه قال : ويكره أن يخطب متكئاً على قوس أو عصا لكن قال في الحاوي القدسي : إذا فرغ المؤذنون قام الإمام والسيف بيساره وهو متكئ عليه اهـ. وهو صريح فيه إلا أن يفرق بين السيف وغيره. وفي المجتبى : ويخطب بالسيف في البلدة التي فتحت بالسيف. وأما الدعاء للسلطان في الخطبة فلا يستحب لما روي أن عطاء سئل عن ذلك فقال : إنه محدث وإنما كانت الخطبة تذكيراً.
As for the khatib, it is required that he be qualified for imamah in Jumu'ah, and the sunnah for him is purity, standing, facing the people with his face, refraining from greeting from the time he exits until he enters the prayer, and refraining from speech. Al-Shafi'i said: When he ascends the minbar, he greets the people. His statement [i.e., al-Shafi'i's] is not [accepted] because when the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech that would invalidate that. It is from the sunnah that the khatib be on a minbar, following the example of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. In al-Mudmarat, citing Rawdat al-'Ulama: The wisdom is that the khatib girds a sword. I heard the jurist Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani say: Every town conquered by force with the sword—the khatib delivers the khutbah on its minbar girded with a sword, showing them that it was conquered by the sword; if you turn back from Islam, then that sword remains in the hands of Muslims; we will fight you with it until you return to Islam. Every town whose people submitted willingly—they deliver the khutbah without a sword. The city of the Prophet ﷺ was conquered by the Qur'an, so the khatib delivers without a sword, and that town is 'ushriyyah (subject to tithe). Mecca was conquered by the sword, so the khatib delivers with a sword. End quote. This indicates that he girds the sword, not that he holds it in his hand as is customary, although the apparent in al-Khulasah is its disapproval, for he said: It is disliked to deliver leaning on a bow or a stick. But al-Hawi al-Qudsi said: When the mu'adhdhins finish, the imam stands with the sword in his left hand leaning on it. End quote. This is explicit about it, unless one differentiates between a sword and other [objects]. In al-Mujtaba: He delivers with a sword in the town conquered by the sword. As for supplication for the ruler in the khutbah, it is not recommended, because it is related that 'Ata was asked about it and said: It is an innovation; the khutbah was only a reminder.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage expands on the qualifications and sunnah practices of the khatib (Friday sermon giver). It first states the minimum requirement: he must be qualified to lead the Jumu'ah prayer (i.e., be a Muslim, male, sane, adult, and knowledgeable). The sunnah for him includes being in a state of purity, standing, facing the congregation, refraining from greeting anyone from the time he leaves his place until he finishes the prayer, and refraining from speaking unnecessarily. A dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is mentioned: al-Shafi'i holds that the khatib should greet the congregation upon ascending the minbar, but the Hanafi position is that greeting is not done because once the imam steps out, all speech is prohibited. The text then discusses the sunnah of the minbar and the tradition of carrying a sword. A lengthy quote from al-Mudmarat explains the symbolism: in cities conquered by force, the khatib girds a sword as a reminder of military strength; in cities that surrendered peacefully, no sword is used. The text clarifies that the sword is worn (girded) not held, and differentiates between leaning on a stick (disliked) and carrying a sword (permitted). Finally, it states that supplicating for the ruler in the khutbah is not recommended, as it is an innovation; the original purpose of the khutbah is spiritual reminder.

Key Terms
الخطيب (al-khaṭīb): The person who delivers the Friday sermon; must be qualified to lead the prayer.
متقلداً بالسيف (mutaqallidan bi al-sayf): Girded with a sword, i.e., wearing a sword belt, not holding it in hand.
الدعاء للسلطان (al-duʿāʾ li al-sulṭān): Supplication for the ruler during the khutbah; considered an innovation (bid'ah) by some early scholars.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khatib must be qualified, observe sunnahs like purity and standing, avoid greeting and speech, and in conquered cities gird a sword as a symbol.

Rulings for the Listener of the Friday Khutbah: Obligations, Sunan, and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Details the obligations and recommended behaviors for those listening to the Friday khutbah, including facing the imam, silence, and avoiding disliked actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunnah and makruh actions for the listener of the Friday khutbah, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on stepping over and salawat, and apply the correct ruling in practice.

Core Idea
The listener's sunnah actions include facing the imam and silence; stepping over is disliked after the imam appears, per the mufta bihi view.

The Friday khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah, and the listener's conduct during it carries specific rulings. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq details the recommended and disliked actions, including an intra-Hanafi dispute on stepping over people and sending salawat. Understanding these distinctions helps you observe the khutbah correctly and know when exceptions apply.

Guided Path
1
List the sunnah and makruh actions for the listener
Identify what the listener is commanded to do (face imam, listen silently) and what is disliked (speaking, eating, fidgeting).
The sunnah includes facing the imam and being silent; speaking is makruh tahrimi.
2
Analyze the dispute on stepping over (takhaffī)
Note Abu Hanifa's absolute dislike versus the Sahibayn's restriction to after the imam's exit. Understand the evidence and al-Razi's mediation.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view: disliked only after the imam comes out.
3
Analyze the dispute on sending salawat
The text says the listener should not send salawat aloud; the Sahibayn allow it in the heart. Recognize this as a minor difference.
Sending salawat silently is permissible.
4
Examine the condition of attending the khutbah
Note that attending the khutbah is a condition (shart) for the imam but not for the follower. This affects validity of Jumu'ah.
The follower's prayer is valid even if he misses part of the khutbah.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: In a given situation, when is stepping over allowed? Also consider the orientation of the listener: sunnah to face imam but common practice to face qibla due to crowding.
The ruling adapts to circumstances without contradicting the sunnah.

وأما المستمع فيستقبل الإمام إذا بدأ بالخطبة وينصت ولا يتكلم ولا يرد السلام ولا يشمت ولا يصلي على النبي . وقالا : يصلي السامع في نفسه، وفي جواز قراءة القرآن وذكر الفقه والنظر فيه لمن يستمع الخطبة اختلاف المشايخ. ويكره لمستمع الخطبة ما يكره في الصلاة كالأكل والشرب والعبث والالتفات، وأما التخطي فمكروه عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : إنما يكره بعد خروج الإمام. وقال الرازي : إنما يجوز قبله إذا لم يؤذ أحداً فأما تخطي السؤال فمكروه في جميع الأحوال بالإجماع وأما شهود الخطبة فشرط في حق الإمام دون المأموم .اهـ. ما في المجتبي . ثم قولهم إن السنة في المستمع استقبال الإمام مخالف لما عليه عمل الناس من استقبال المستمع للقبلة ولهذا قال في التجنيس والرسم في زماننا أن القوم يستقبلون القبلة قال : لأنهم لو استقبلوا الإمام الخرجوا في تسوية الصفوف بعد فراغه لكثرة الزحام. وجزم في الخلاصة بأنه يستحب استقباله إن كان أمام الإمام، فإن كان عن يمين الإمام أو عن يساره قريباً من الإمام ينحرف إلى الإمام مستعداً للسماع. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها : الدنو من الإمام أفضل من التباعد على الصحيح ومنهم من اختار التباعد حتى لا يسمع مدح الظلمة في الخطبة، ولهذا اختار بعضهم أن الخطيب ما دام في الحمد والمواعظ فعليهم الاستماع فإذا أخذ في مدح الظلمة والثناء عليهم فلا بأس بالكلام حينئذ. وحكى في الظهيرية والخانية عن إبراهيم النخعي وإبراهيم بن مهاجر أنهما كانا يتكلمان وقت الخطبة، فقيل لإبراهيم النخعي في فقال : إني صليت الظهر في داري ثم رحت إلى الجمعة ثقية ولذلك تأويلان: أحدهما أن الناس كانوا في ذلك الزمان :فريقين : فريق منهم لا يصلي الجمعة لأنه كان لا يرى الجائر سلطاناً وسلطانهم يومئذ كان جائراً فإنهم كانوا لا يصلون الجمعة من أجل ذلك، وكان فريق منهم يترك الجمعة لأن السلطان كان يؤخر الجمعة عن وقتها في ذلك الزمان فكانوا يأتون الظهر في دارهم ثم يصلون مع الإمام ويجعلونها سبحة أي نافلة .اهـ. وقد سمعت في زماننا أن بعضهم يترك الجمعة متأولاً بالتأويل الأول وهو فاسد لأن فاعله مجتهد رأى ذلك. وأما المقلد لأبي حنيفة فحرام عليه ذلك لأن مذهب إمامه أن الجائر سلطان كما قدمناه .
As for the listener, he faces the imam when he begins the khutbah, listens attentively, does not speak, does not return the greeting, does not say yarhamuk Allah, and does not send salawat upon the Prophet. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The listener sends salawat in his heart. Regarding the permissibility of reciting the Qur'an and mentioning fiqh and reflecting upon it for the one listening to the khutbah—there is disagreement among the mashayikh. Disliked for the listener are things disliked in prayer, such as eating, drinking, fidgeting, and turning away. As for stepping over people, it is disliked according to Abu Hanifa. The two said: It is only disliked after the imam comes out. Al-Razi said: It is permitted before that if he does not harm anyone. As for stepping over for asking (for charity?), it is disliked in all circumstances by consensus. And attending the khutbah is a condition for the imam, not for the ma'mum. End of what is in al-Mujtaba. Then their statement that the sunnah for the listener is to face the imam contradicts what people practice: facing the qibla. Therefore, it was said in al-Tajnīs: The current practice in our time is that the people face the qibla, because if they faced the imam, they would disrupt the straightening of the rows after he finishes due to great crowding. Al-Khulasah decisively stated that it is recommended to face him if he is in front of the imam; if he is to the right or left of the imam, close to the imam, he turns toward the imam, ready to listen. In al-Khulasah and others: Proximity to the imam is better than distance, according to the sound view. Some chose distance so as not to hear the praise of oppressors in the khutbah. Hence, some chose that as long as the khatib is in praise and admonitions, they should listen; if he begins to praise oppressors and commend them, then there is no harm in speaking at that time. In al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya, it is narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Ibrahim ibn Muhajir that they used to speak during the khutbah. It was said to Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, [and he replied]: 'I prayed zuhr in my house and then went to Jumu'ah as a safeguard.' There are two interpretations: One is that people at that time were two groups: a group did not pray Jumu'ah because they did not consider the unjust ruler a legitimate ruler, and their ruler at that time was unjust; so they did not pray Jumu'ah for that reason. Another group left Jumu'ah because the ruler delayed it from its time; they would pray zuhr in their houses and then pray with the imam, making it a supererogatory (nāfilah) prayer. End quote. I have heard in our time that some leave Jumu'ah interpreting with the first interpretation, which is corrupt, because the doer is a mujtahid holding that view. As for a muqallid of Abu Hanifa, it is forbidden for him to do that, because the madhhab of his imam is that the unjust ruler is still a ruler, as we have mentioned earlier.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage covers the rulings for the listener (mustami') during the Friday khutbah. It begins by stating the recommended acts: facing the imam, listening attentively, not speaking, not returning greetings, not saying yarhamuk Allah, and not sending salawat on the Prophet. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the listener may send salawat in his heart without speaking. There is also a difference of opinion among scholars about reciting Qur'an or studying fiqh during the khutbah. The text then lists actions disliked during the khutbah, analogous to those disliked in prayer, such as eating, drinking, and fidgeting. The issue of stepping over people (takhaffī) is discussed: Abu Hanifa holds it is disliked absolutely; the Sahibayn say it is disliked only after the imam comes out; al-Razi says it is permitted before that if no one is harmed. The text then discusses the condition of attending the khutbah: it is a condition for the validity of the Jumu'ah prayer for the imam but not for the followers. Next, there is a discussion about the orientation of the listener: the sunnah is to face the imam, but common practice is to face the qibla due to crowding. Al-Khulasah clarifies that if the listener is directly in front of the imam, he should face him; if to the side, he should turn slightly towards the imam. Proximity to the imam is preferable, but some avoid it to not hear praise of unjust rulers; in such cases, speaking is allowed when the khatib praises oppressors. Finally, a narration about Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Ibn Muhajir is given: they used to speak during the khutbah, explaining that they had already prayed zuhr as a precaution. Two interpretations are provided, and the commentator warns that today's muqallids of Abu Hanifa cannot abandon Jumu'ah on such grounds.

Key Terms
المستمع (al-mustamiʿ): The person listening to the Friday khutbah; subject to specific rules of silence and orientation.
التخطي (al-takhaṭṭī): Stepping over people's shoulders to reach a forward row in the mosque.
شهود الخطبة (shuhūd al-khuṭbah): Attendance at the Friday sermon; a condition (shart) for the imam, not the follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) It is disliked only before the imam comes out

Key Takeaway
The listener's conduct during the Friday khutbah includes sunnah actions (facing imam, silence) and makruh actions (speaking, stepping over after imam's exit); intra-Hanafi differences are resolved by al-Razi's mediation.

Balancing Fear and Hope in the Khutbah
Ruling with proof on khutbah content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended balance between fear and hope in the Friday sermon and identify the sunnah act of seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) before the khutbah.

Core Idea
The Friday sermon must balance fear and hope; seeking refuge silently before it is a sunnah.

The Friday khutbah is a powerful platform to guide the congregation. This lesson explores the classical Hanafi recommendations for its content — neither too frightening nor too comforting — and the quiet preparation of seeking refuge with Allah before ascending the minbar. You will also learn a subtle linguistic distinction that prevents confusion with marriage proposals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core recommendation
Read the first opinion: the preacher's session should contain both fear (khawf) and hope (raja'). Note the reason: extremes lead to despair or false security.
2
Examine the proof
Al-Rustughfani cites the hadith 'Make things easy...' to support emphasizing mercy and hope. Understand how this hadith is used to justify a hopeful tone.
The hadith is a general principle, not specifically about khutbah.
3
Recognize the sunnah of ta'awwudh
Abu Yusuf recommends that the khatib seek refuge with Allah silently before beginning the khutbah. This is a recommended practice (sunnah).
The silent seeking is essential — not aloud.
4
Differentiate the linguistic nuance
Note the difference: khutbah (with dammah) means sermon; khitbah (with kasrah) means proposal of marriage. This avoids confusion in textual interpretation.
The Qur'anic reference uses the kasrah form for marriage proposal.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf on a discerning boy
The passage ends with a disagreement about a discerning boy. Understand that this refers to whether such a boy can lead prayer or deliver khutbah — a separate issue not fully elaborated here.
Shaykh Isma'il reports the majority permits it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي أول التجنيس معزياً إلى الفقيه أبي الليث : ينبغي أن يكون في مجلس الواعظ الخوف والرجاء ولا يجعل كله خوفاً ولا كله رجاء لأنه ورد النهي عن ذلك، ولأن الأول يفضي إلى القنوط ، والثاني إلى الأمن فيجمع بينهما. وقال الإمام أبو بكر الرستغفني : يجب أن يتكلم في الرحمة والرجاء لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام يسروا ولا تعسروا، وبشروا ولا تنفروا»(۱) ولأن من رجع إلى الباب بالكرامة يكون أثبت .اهـ. وفي القنية قال أبو يوسف في الجامع : ينبغي للخطيب إذا صعد المنبر أن يتعوذ بالله في نفسه قبل الخطبة .اهـ. وفي ضياء الحلوم مختصر شمس العلوم : خطب على المنبر خطبة - بضم الخاء - وخطب المرأة خطبة بكسر الخاء . قال الله تعالى من خطبة النساء اختلف المشايخ فيه والخلاف في صبي يعقل ا هـ. فما هنا على أحد القولين وما سيأتي عن المجتبى مبني على الآخر . قال الشيخ إسماعيل : والأكثر على الجواز.
In the beginning of al-Tajnīs, citing the jurist Abu al-Layth: The preacher's session should contain fear and hope, and should not be entirely fear nor entirely hope, because prohibition of that has been reported, and because the first leads to despair and the second to security, so combine both. Imam Abu Bakr al-Rustughfani said: He must speak about mercy and hope, due to his ﷺ saying: 'Make things easy, do not make things difficult; give glad tidings, do not repulse.' And because one who returns to the door with honor is more steadfast. End quote. In al-Qunyah, Abu Yusuf said in al-Jami': The khatib, when he ascends the minbar, should seek refuge with Allah in himself before the khutbah. End quote. In Diya' al-Hulum, abridgment of Shams al-'Ulum: He delivered a khutbah on the minbar—with dammah on the khā'—and he proposed to a woman (khataba al-mar'ah) with kasrah on the khā'. Allah said: '...from the proposal of women...' The mashayikh disagreed about it, and the disagreement involves a discerning boy. End quote. So what is here is based on one of the two sayings, and what will come from al-Mujtaba is built on the other. Shaykh Isma'il said: The majority lean towards permissibility.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage concludes the chapter on Friday prayer with several important points about the content and preparation of the khutbah. First, it quotes al-Tajnīs citing Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: the preacher should balance fear (takhwīf) and hope (tarjī'), not go to extremes, as extremes lead to despair or false security. Imam Abu Bakr al-Rustughfani emphasizes mercy and hope, citing the hadith 'Make things easy, do not make things difficult' and noting that a person returning with honor is more steadfast. Then from al-Qunyah, Abu Yusuf recommends that the khatib seek refuge (ta'awwudh) in Allah silently before beginning the khutbah. Finally, a linguistic note from Diya' al-Hulum distinguishes two words: khutbah (with dammah) meaning sermon, and khitbah (with kasrah) meaning proposal of marriage. The text then mentions a disagreement among scholars regarding a discerning boy (ṣabī yaʿqil) and the permissibility of something (likely his leading the prayer or delivering the khutbah?). The commentator notes that his current explanation follows one view, and a later passage from al-Mujtaba follows the other; Shaykh Isma'il reports that the majority permit it.

Key Terms
الخوف والرجاء (al-khawf wa al-rajāʾ): Fear of Allah's punishment and hope in His mercy; both should be present in the sermon.
التعوذ (al-taʿawwudh): Seeking refuge in Allah (saying a'udhu billah) silently before beginning the khutbah.
صبي يعقل (ṣabī yaʿqil): A boy who has reached the age of discernment (about seven years), able to understand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Greet the congregation with salam

Key Takeaway
The Friday sermon must combine fear and hope, and the khatib is recommended to silently seek refuge before starting.

Rulings on the Khatib and the Friday Sermon: Sword, Supplication, Seating, and Speaking
Commentary expanding on multiple rulings related to the Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the khatib's use of a sword, supplication for the ruler, preference for seating, and permissibility of speaking during the Friday sermon.

Core Idea
The Friday sermon's details are governed by custom and political context, not fixed wajib elements.

The Friday sermon is wajib, but many details about the khatib's actions and the congregation's conduct are subject to ikhtilaf and custom. This passage from Bahr al-Rā’iq expands upon the base text of Kanz al-Daqā’iq, clarifying when a sword is used, whether to supplicate for the ruler, how to sit, and when speaking is permitted. Understanding these nuances prevents either excessive rigor or neglect of the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from Kanz al-Daqā’iq
The base matn states: 'The khatib without a sword, and that town being 'ushriyya (conquered peacefully), and Makkah was conquered by sword, so he delivers the sermon with a sword.' Recognise that this is a concise ruling linking sword use to the method of conquest.
This is the foundation upon which the commentator builds.
2
Follow the commentator's expansion on the sword
The commentator clarifies that the sword is worn on the shoulder, not held in hand. He then contrasts leaning on a sword (permitted) with leaning on a bow or staff (disliked), citing al-Khulāsa and al-Hāwī al-Qudsī. Understand that the sword is a symbol specific to towns conquered by force.
Note the intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars differentiate between sword and other objects.
3
Examine the ruling on supplication for the ruler
The text from al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj states that supplication (du'ā') for the ruler is not mustahabb because it is an innovation (muhdath). The original purpose of the sermon is tadhkīr (reminder). Recognise that the evidence is a narration from 'Aṭā'.
This ruling contrasts with common practice in some times and places.
4
Analyze the ikhtilāf on seating and speaking during the sermon
The passage presents two views: sitting near the imam is better, but some prefer distance to avoid hearing praise of tyrants. Speaking is generally prohibited during the sermon, but becomes permissible when the khatib praises oppressors. Understand the principle that the congregation's duty to listen is contingent on the content.
This reflects the realpolitik of the time and the concept of taqiyya.
5
Understand the taqiyya-related exceptions and the warning
Ibrāhīm al-Nakha'ī spoke during the sermon, justifying it as taqiyya and having already prayed Zuhr. The commentator warns against using this to abandon Friday prayer, because the Hanafi position is that the unjust ruler is still a sultan and Friday with him is valid.
This step reinforces the importance of following the relied-upon (muftā bihī) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٦٠ كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة الجمعة الخطيب بلا سيف وتكون تلك البلدة عشرية ومكة فتحت بالسيف فيخطب مع السيف اهـ . وهذا مفيد لكونه يتقلد بالسيف لا أنه يمسكه بيده كما هو المتعارف مع أن ظاهر ما في الخلاصة كراهة ذلك فإنه قال : ويكره أن يخطب متكئاً على قوس أو عصا لكن قال في الحاوي القدسي : إذا فرغ المؤذنون قام الإمام والسيف بيساره وهو متكئ عليه اهـ. وهو صريح فيه إلا أن يفرق بين السيف وغيره. وفي المجتبى : ويخطب بالسيف في البلدة التي فتحت بالسيف. وفي السراج الوهاج وأما الدعاء للسلطان في الخطبة فلا يستحب لما روي أن عطاء سئل عن ذلك فقال : إنه محدث وإنما كانت الخطبة تذكيراً. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها : الدنو من الإمام أفضل من التباعد على الصحيح ومنهم من اختار التباعد حتى لا يسمع مدح الظلمة في الخطبة، ولهذا اختار بعضهم أن الخطيب ما دام في الحمد والمواعظ فعليهم الاستماع فإذا أخذ في مدح الظلمة والثناء عليهم فلا بأس بالكلام حينئذ. وحكى في الظهيرية والخانية عن إبراهيم النخعي وإبراهيم بن مهاجر أنهما كانا يتكلمان وقت الخطبة، فقيل لإبراهيم النخعي في فقال : إني صليت الظهر في داري ثم رحت إلى الجمعة تقية ولذلك تأويلان: أحدهما أن الناس كانوا في ذلك الزمان فريقين: فريق منهم لا يصلي الجمعة لأنه كان لا يرى الجائر سلطاناً وسلطانهم يومئذ كان جائراً فإنهم كانوا لا يصلون الجمعة من أجل ذلك، وكان فريق منهم يترك الجمعة لأن السلطان كان يؤخر الجمعة عن وقتها في ذلك الزمان فكانوا يأتون الظهر في دارهم ثم يصلون مع الإمام ويجعلونها سبحة أي نافلة .اهـ. وقد سمعت في زماننا أن بعضهم يترك الجمعة متأولاً بالتأويل الأول وهو فاسد لأن فاعله مجتهد رأى ذلك. وأما المقلد لأبي حنيفة فحرام عليه ذلك لأن مذهب إمامه أن الجائر سلطان كما قدمناه .
The khatib without a sword, and that town being a tithed (conquered peacefully), while Makkah was conquered by sword, so he delivers the sermon with a sword, end. And this is useful that he wears/carries the sword on his shoulder, not that he holds it in his hand as is conventional, although the apparent meaning in al-Khulasa is dislike of that, for he said: It is disliked that he delivers the sermon leaning on a bow or staff. But al-Hawi al-Qudsi said: When the mu'adhdhins finish, the imam stands with the sword in his left hand, leaning on it, end. And it is explicit in that, unless one differentiates between sword and other things. And in al-Mujtaba: He delivers the sermon with a sword in the town conquered by sword. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: As for supplication for the ruler in the sermon, it is not recommended, because it is narrated that 'Ata' was asked about that and said: It is an innovation; the sermon was only a reminder. And in al-Khulasa and others: Being near the imam is better than being distant on the correct view, and among them are those who chose distance so as not to hear praise of tyrants in the sermon. For this reason, some chose that as long as the khatib is in praise (of Allah) and exhortations, they must listen; but when he starts praising tyrants and extolling them, then there is no harm in speaking at that time. And it is narrated in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Ibrahim ibn Muhajir that they used to speak during the sermon. It was said to Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and he said: I prayed Zuhr in my house, then I went to Friday prayer out of dissimulation (taqiyya). And for that there are two interpretations: One is that the people at that time were two groups: a group who did not pray Friday because they did not consider the unjust ruler as a sultan, and their ruler at that time was unjust, so they did not pray Friday for that reason; and a group who abandoned Friday because the ruler used to delay Friday from its time in that era, so they would pray Zuhr in their homes then pray with the imam and make it a supererogatory (nafl) prayer. End. And I have heard in our time that some abandon Friday with the first interpretation, which is corrupt because the doer is a mujtahid who saw that. As for the muqallid of Abu Hanifa, it is forbidden for him because his imam's madhhab is that the unjust (ruler) is a sultan as we have presented.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents multiple rulings related to the Friday sermon (khatba) and the khatib. First, it discusses whether the khatib should hold a sword. The text clarifies that in towns conquered peacefully ('ushriyya), no sword is needed, but in Makkah (conquered by force), the khatib should deliver the sermon with a sword. However, it notes a difference of opinion: some texts indicate the sword is carried on the shoulder, not held in hand, and leaning on a sword is distinguished from leaning on a bow or staff, which is disliked. Second, supplication for the ruler in the sermon is not recommended (mustahabb) because it is an innovation; the original purpose of the sermon is reminder (tadhkir). Third, the preferred seating is near the imam, unless one fears hearing praise of tyrants, in which case distance is acceptable; speaking is permissible only when the khatib engages in praise of oppressors. Fourth, the text reports that Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and others spoke during the sermon, interpreting this as taqiyya (dissimulation) or having prayed Zuhr first as a precaution. The author warns against abandoning Friday prayer based on the view that the ruler is unjust, because the Hanafi position is that the unjust is still a sultan and Friday with him is valid.

Key Terms
خطيب (khatib): The person delivering the Friday sermon; the imam or a representative.
سيف (sayf): Sword; a symbol of authority in towns conquered by force.
الخطبة (khutba): The sermon; a wajib part of Friday prayer consisting of praise of Allah, exhortation, etc.
تقيَّة (taqiyya): Dissimulation; acting against one's true beliefs to protect oneself from harm.
عشريَّة (ushriyya): A town conquered peacefully, where land remains subject to tithe ('ushr) rather than kharāj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi texts cited, what is the ruling on the khatib leaning on a bow during the Friday sermon?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah
C) It is makruh
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
The Friday sermon has fixed pillars, but many details (sword, supplication, seating) are sunnah or makruh, subject to ikhtilaf and contextual custom.

The Eight Sermons and Their Prescribed Openings: Tahmid and Takbir
Classifies eight sermons and their openings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the eight types of sermons recognized in the Hanafi school and state whether each begins with Tahmid or Takbir.

Core Idea
Friday, marriage, and rain sermons begin with Tahmid; Eid and Hajj sermons begin with Takbir.

In the Hanafi school, the type of sermon dictates how it should begin. Knowing which sermons open with Tahmid (praise of Allah) versus Takbir (declaration of Allah's greatness) is essential for the khatib to follow the sunnah correctly. This passage from Khizanat al-Fiqh provides the definitive classification.

Guided Path
1
List the eight sermons
Identify all eight sermons mentioned in the passage: Friday, two Eids, marriage, rain (istisqa), and three Hajj sermons (in Makkah, Arafat, and Mina).
The rain sermon is included according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Abu Hanifa's view may differ.
2
Divide into two groups by opening
Separate the sermons into those that begin with Tahmid (Friday, Istisqa, Nikah) and those that begin with Takbir (Eidain and the three Hajj sermons).
The Hajj sermons in Makkah and Arafat also include Talbiyah after Takbir.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that the rain sermon is considered a sermon only in the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Abu Hanifa's position is not explicitly stated but implied as different.
This affects whether a khatib should deliver a separate sermon for rain.
4
Apply the ruling
When preparing any of these sermons, ensure the opening formula matches the type: Tahmid for Friday, Nikah, and Istisqa; Takbir for Eids and Hajj.
For Hajj sermons, also include Talbiyah after Takbir.

And that: In al-Tajnis, with attribution to al-Faqih Abu al-Layth: It is proper that in the assembly of the preacher there be fear and hope, and not make it all fear nor all hope because prohibition came about that, and because the first leads to despair, and the second to security (from punishment), so he combines both. And Imam Abu Bakr al-Rustaghnani said: He must speak about mercy and hope due to his (SAW) saying: 'Make things easy, not difficult; give glad tidings, do not repel.' And because one who returns to the door with honor is more established. End. And in al-Qunyah, Abu Yusuf said in al-Jami': The khatib, when he ascends the minbar, should seek refuge with Allah in himself before the sermon. End. And in Diya' al-Huloom Mukhtasar Shams al-Ulum: He delivered a sermon on the minbar: 'khutba' with dammah on kha', and he proposed to a woman: 'khutba' with kasrah on kha'. Allah said: 'concerning the proposal of women' (2:235). The scholars differed about it, and the difference is concerning a boy who understands. End. So what is here is on one of the two opinions, and what will come from al-Mujtaba is based on the other. Sheikh Ismail said: The majority are on permissibility. (1) Narrated by Bukhari in Kitab al-Ilm Bab ... etc. [PAGE_261] Kitab al-Salah, Bab Salat al-Jumu'ah: 'A single praise or tahleel or tasbeeh and the congregation being three besides the imam, if they depart before his sajdah' (2:235) and in the hadith: 'None of you should propose (to a woman) over the proposal of his brother' (2). End. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: It is sunnah that the imam's sitting in his chamber be on the right side of the minbar; if not, then in its direction or side. And it is disliked that he pray in the mihrab before the sermon. And he should wear black in emulation of the caliphs and due to inheritance in ages and cities. End. And I have not seen in the books of our imams regarding the ruling of the stairway (marqi) from which the khatib exits his chamber and recites the verse as is customary, whether it is sunnah or not. And in al-Bada'i': It is disliked for the khatib to speak during his sermon unless it is commanding good, then it is not disliked because it is part of it. And in Khizanat al-Fiqh by Abu al-Layth: The sermons are eight: Friday sermon, Eid al-Fitr sermon, Eid al-Adha sermon, marriage sermon, and sermon for rain (istisqa') according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and three sermons in Hajj: one without sitting in Makkah before the day of Tarwiyya after Zuhr, the second in Arafat before Zuhr with a light sitting, and the third after the day of Nahr (sacrifice) by one day in Mina, delivering one sermon after Zuhr. He begins three of them with Tahmid: Friday, Istisqa', and marriage sermons; and five with Takbir: Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three Hajj sermons, except that the sermons in Makkah and Arafat begin with Takbir then Talbiyah then the sermon. End.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage expands on various aspects of sermons (khutab). It begins with general advice for preachers to balance fear and hope, citing a hadith to make matters easy. It includes a narration from Abu Yusuf that the khatib should seek refuge in Allah silently before the sermon. It then clarifies a linguistic point: 'khutba' (with dammah) means a sermon, while 'khutba' (with kasrah) means a marriage proposal. The passage then lists the eight types of sermons recognized in the Hanafi school: Friday, two Eids, marriage, rain (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and three Hajj sermons (in Makkah, Arafat, and Mina). It specifies which sermons begin with Tahmid (praise of Allah) and which begin with Takbir (saying Allahu Akbar). Notably, Friday, rain, and marriage sermons start with Tahmid; the rest start with Takbir. The Hajj sermons in Makkah and Arafat also begin with Takbir followed by Talbiyah. This classification is important for knowing the proper sunnah format of each sermon.

Key Terms
التحميد (tahmid): Saying 'Alhamdulillah' (praise be to Allah); the prescribed opening for certain sermons.
التكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; the opening for Eid and Hajj sermons.
التلبية (talbiyah): Saying 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...'; only in Hajj sermons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Friday and Eid sermons
B) Eid and marriage sermons
C) Eid and Hajj sermons
D) Friday and rain sermons

Key Takeaway
Friday, marriage, and rain sermons begin with Tahmid; Eid and Hajj sermons begin with Takbir.

Minimum Friday Sermon: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimal valid Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the minimum Friday sermon and evaluate their respective evidences.

Core Idea
The Friday sermon is valid with any dhikr according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn require a customary speech.

The Friday sermon is a vital condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. But what is the minimum required? This lesson unpacks an important intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any deliberate remembrance of Allah suffices, while his two chief disciples require a speech that customarily qualifies as a sermon. We will trace the evidence and reasoning behind each position, exploring how the Hanafi school balances definitive texts with customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
Read the passage and note the exact ruling: what is the minimum content of the Friday sermon according to Abu Hanifa versus the Sahibayn?
The disagreement is over the condition (shart) of content, not the obligation of the sermon itself.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his evidence
Abu Hanifa says any deliberate dhikr suffices. Locate his dalil: the absolute Qur'anic command to remember Allah. What is the thubut and dalala of this evidence?
The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in implication, yet Abu Hanifa treats it as primary.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
The two disciples require speech customarily called a khutbah, minimum length of tashahhud. Their dalil is the customary practice ('urf) and Prophetic sunnah.
They restrict the absolute command by what is conventionally recognized.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa differentiates between the definitive (qat'i) text and the speculative (zanni) practice. The verse makes absolute dhikr fard; the Prophet's longer sermon establishes sunnah, not obligation.
This is a key usul principle: the qat'i text cannot be overridden by zanni custom.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practically, if a khatib only says 'Alhamdulillah', the prayer is valid per Abu Hanifa but invalid per the Sahibayn. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The story of Caliph Uthman supports the permissibility of the minimum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وكفت تحميدة أو تم ليلة أو تسبيحة أي وكفى في الخطبة المفروضة مطلق ذكر الله تعالى على وجه القصد عند أبي حنيفة لإطلاقه في الآية الشريفة. وقالا : الشرط أن يأتي بكلام يسمى خطبة في العرف. وأقله قدر التشهد إلى عبده ورسوله تقييداً له بالمتعارف كما قالاه في القراءة. وأبو حنيفة عمل بالقاطع والظني فقال بافتراض مطلق الذكر للآية وباستنان الخطبة المتعارفة لفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام تنزيلاً للمشروعات على حسب أدلتها ، ويؤيده قصة عثمان المذكورة في كتب الفقه وهي أنه لما خطب في أول جمعة ولي الخلافة صعد المنبر فقال : الحمد الله فارتج عليه فقال : إن أبا بكر وعمر كانا يعدان لهذا المقام مقالاً وأنتم
His saying: 'And a single praise or tahleel or tasbeeh is sufficient' means that in the obligatory sermon, any remembrance of Allah intended as such is sufficient according to Abu Hanifa, due to its absolute mention in the noble verse. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The condition is that he comes with speech that is called a sermon in custom. And its minimum is the amount of the tashahhud up to 'wa 'abdihi wa rasulihi', restricting it to what is customary, as they said regarding recitation. Abu Hanifa acted upon the definitive (qat'i) and the speculative (zanni), making obligatory absolute dhikr due to the verse, and making the customary sermon sunnah due to his (SAW) action, placing the legislated acts according to their evidences. And it is supported by the story of Uthman mentioned in fiqh books: when he delivered the sermon in the first Friday after his caliphate, he ascended the minbar and said 'Alhamdulillah' and then he faltered, and he said: 'Abu Bakr and 'Umar used to prepare a speech for this occasion, but you...'
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum content of the Friday sermon. The issue arises from the commentary on the line 'وكفت تحميدة أو تهليلة أو تسبيحة' (a single praise, or tahleel, or tasbeeh suffices). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, any deliberate remembrance of Allah (dhikr) is sufficient for the obligatory sermon, based on the absolute command in the Qur'an (such as 'and remember Allah much' or similar). The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, condition that the words must constitute something customarily recognized as a sermon (khutba). They set the minimum at the equivalent of the tashahhud up to 'wa 'abdihi wa rasulihi', which is a common benchmark. Abu Hanifa's method distinguishes between the definitive (qat'i) text and the speculative (zanni) practice: the verse makes absolute dhikr obligatory (fard), while the Prophet's actual sunnah of delivering a longer sermon establishes the recommended (sunnah) form. Thus, if one only says 'Alhamdulillah' intending the sermon, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the sunnah is to give a more comprehensive sermon. The story of Caliph Uthman, who once only managed 'Alhamdulillah' due to forgetfulness, supports Abu Hanifa's view that this suffices, as the prayer would have been valid.

Key Terms
تحميدة (tahmeedah): A single utterance of 'Alhamdulillah' (praise be to Allah).
تهليلة (tahleelah): A single utterance of 'La ilaha illa Allah' (There is no god but Allah).
التشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in prayer; here used as a measure of length.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum sufficient for the Friday sermon according to Abu Hanifa?
A) A speech equal to tashahhud
B) A single praise (tahmeedah) or similar dhikr
C) Recitation of a long verse
D) A sermon of about ten minutes

Key Takeaway
The Friday sermon is valid with any deliberate dhikr (Abu Hanifa's view, mufta bihi), but the sunnah is a full customary sermon.

Sufficiency of a Single Dhikr for the Friday Sermon
Dispute on what constitutes a valid khutbah: minimal dhikr vs. conventional sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimal requirement for the Friday khutbah according to Abu Hanifa and explain the proof from the Quran and the consensus of the Companions.

Core Idea
A single intentional dhikr suffices for the obligatory Friday sermon; the customary sermon is sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what constitutes a valid Friday sermon? The source passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents Abu Hanifa's view that any deliberate remembrance of Allah is sufficient, based on the absolute command in Surah al-Jumu'ah, while his two disciples require a conventional sermon. We will unpack the proofs, the supporting story of 'Uthman, and the important distinction of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
What is the act under discussion? (the Friday khutbah) What is the dispute? (minimum content that fulfills the obligation)
The khutbah itself is wajib; the dispute is on its minimal valid form.
2
Locate Abu Hanifa's primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse cited and how it is used to prove that any dhikr suffices.
Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9 commands 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (dhikr).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
How does the absolute word 'dhikr' in the verse prove that a single phrase qualifies?
The term is unqualified ('amm), so it includes all forms of remembrance.
4
Examine the opposition's proof and Abu Hanifa's response
What do the Sahibayn argue? (customary definition of khutbah) How does Abu Hanifa counter? (distinction between obligatory and sunnah, and story of 'Uthman)
The Sahibayn restrict the absolute command by custom (urf), which Abu Hanifa considers a secondary evidence.
5
Evaluate the supporting evidence: the story of 'Uthman
How does the incident of 'Uthman being unable to continue his sermon and descending without objection serve as evidence of consensus?
The companions' silence is considered tacit approval (ijma suktuti).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وكفت تحميدة أو تم ليلة أو تسبيحة أي وكفى في الخطبة المفروضة مطلق ذكر الله تعالى على وجه القصد عند أبي حنيفة لإطلاقه في الآية الشريفة. وقالا : الشرط أن يأتي بكلام يسمى خطبة في العرف. وأقله قدر التشهد إلى عبده ورسوله تقييداً له بالمتعارف كما قالاه في القراءة. وأبو حنيفة عمل بالقاطع والظني فقال بافتراض مطلق الذكر للآية وباستنان الخطبة المتعارفة لفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام تنزيلاً للمشروعات على حسب أدلتها ، ويؤيده قصة عثمان المذكورة في كتب الفقه وهي أنه لما خطب في أول جمعة ولي الخلافة صعد المنبر فقال : الحمد الله فارتج عليه فقال : إن أبا بكر وعمر كانا يعدان لهذا المقام مقالاً وأنتم وصلى بهم . إلى إمام فعال أحوج منكم إلى إمام ،قوال، وستأتيكم الخطب بعد وأستغفر الله لي ولكم ونزل ولم ينكر عليه أحد منهم فكان إجماعاً. وارتج بالتخفيف على الأصح أي استغلق عليه الخطبة فلم يقدر على إتمامها كذا في المغرب ومراد عثمان بقوله «إنكم إلى إمام إلى آخره» أن الخلفاء الذين يأتون بعد الخلفاء الراشدين تكون على كثرة المقال مع قبح الفعال فأنا وإن لم أكن قوالاً مثلهم فأنا على الخير دون الشر، فأما أن يريد بهذا القول تفضيل نفسه على الشيخين فلا. كذا في النهاية : قيدنا الخطبة بالمفروضة لأن المسنونة لا يكفي فيها مطلقه بل لا بد أن يأتي بما قدمناه . وقيدنا بالقصد لأنه لو عطس على المنبر فقال الحمد لله على عطاسه لا ينوب عن الخطبة عند أبي حنيفة أيضاً كما في التسمية على الذبيحة وعن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى أنه يجزئه، والفرق على هذه الرواية وهو أن المأمور به في الخطبة الذكر مطلقاً لقوله تعالى فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله ﴾ [الجمعة: ۹] وقد وجد وفي باب الذبيحة المأمور الذكر عليه وذلك بأن يقصده والأول أصح . كذا في التنجيس
He said: (And suffice a single tahmid, or tahlil, or tasbih) i.e., in the obligatory khutbah, any mention of Allah intended deliberately suffices according to Abu Hanifa, due to the absolute nature of the noble verse. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The condition is to deliver speech called a khutbah in custom. Its minimum is the amount of tashahhud up to 'and His messenger', restricting it to the customary, as they said in recitation. Abu Hanifa acted on the decisive and the probable, so he held obligatory an absolute dhikr due to the verse, and held the customary khutbah as sunnah due to his action, peace be upon him, basing legislated matters on their evidences. The story of 'Uthman supports this, as mentioned in fiqh books: when he gave the first Friday sermon after becoming caliph, he ascended the minbar and said 'al-hamdu lillah' and then was unable to continue (irtaja). He said: 'Abu Bakr and 'Umar used to prepare speech for this occasion, and you are in need of an active imam more than an eloquent one, and sermons will come to you after. I seek forgiveness of Allah for me and you.' He descended and no one objected, so it was consensus. ... We restricted it to the obligatory khutbah because the supererogatory one does not suffice with mere dhikr; rather one must come with what we mentioned. And we restricted it to intentionality because if he sneezes on the minbar and says 'al-hamdu lillah' for his sneeze, it does not substitute for the khutbah according to Abu Hanifa as well, like the tasmiyah on the animal. The first view is more correct. That is from al-Tanjis.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the minimal requirement for the Friday sermon. It addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that a single dhikr (tahmid, tahlil, or tasbih) suffices for the obligatory khutbah, relying on the absolute command in Quran 62:9 ('hasten to the remembrance of Allah'). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require a proper sermon as conventionally understood, with a minimum like the tashahhud. Abu Hanifa's position is supported by the story of 'Uthman, whose minimal khutbah was accepted by the companions, indicating consensus. The commentary also clarifies that the ruling is only for the obligatory khutbah; supererogatory khutbahs require more. Additionally, intention is necessary: an accidental dhikr (like a sneeze) does not count. The author sides with Abu Hanifa, noting that the first view is the most correct.

Key Terms
تحميدة (tahmidah): A single instance of saying 'al-hamdu lillah' (praise to Allah).
تهليلة (tahlilah): A single utterance of 'la ilaha illa Allah'.
تسبيحة (tasbihah): A single utterance of 'subhan Allah' (glory to Allah).
ارتج (irtaja): To become unable to continue speech; to have a mental block.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum requirement for the Friday sermon (khutbah)?
A) A speech containing praise of Allah, shahada, and blessing on the Prophet
B) Any single phrase of dhikr like 'al-hamdu lillah' or 'subhan Allah' intended as khutbah
C) A minimum of three verses from the Quran
D) The same as the tashahhud in prayer

Key Takeaway
A single intentional dhikr is sufficient for the obligatory Friday sermon according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Minimum Congregation for Friday Prayer: Three Beyond Imam
Determination of the required number of participants for the validity of Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of followers required for Friday prayer according to the Hanafi school, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and apply the rule to determine who counts.

Core Idea
Friday prayer requires a congregation; the Hanafi school sets the minimum at three followers besides the imam.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a key condition for the validity of Friday prayer: the size of the congregation. The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states that the congregation consists of three persons besides the imam, reflecting the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, Abu Yusuf holds that two followers suffice. The text also clarifies who is eligible to form this congregation and who is excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the dispute
The matn states three besides imam; Abu Yusuf says two. Note the exact numbers and that the imam is not counted.
2
Understand the proof
The condition of congregation must be fulfilled for each person, requiring at least three others besides oneself. This is the argument of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
3
Determine who is included
Slaves, travelers, sick, illiterate, and mute are included because they can lead Friday prayer. Women and boys are excluded: women by grammatical gender, boys because they are not complete men.
The absolute term 'three' is restricted to males.
4
Apply the ruling to attendees
The three do not need to have attended the khutbah if they come later; the prayer is valid for them.
This shows that the condition is about the prayer itself, not the khutbah attendance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والجماعة وهم ثلاثة) أي شرط صحتها أن يصلي مع الإمام ثلاثة فأكثر لإجماع العلماء على أنه لا بد فيها من الجماعة كما في البدائع. وإنما اختلفوا في مقدارها فما ذكره المصنف قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : اثنان سوى الإمام لأنهما مع الإمام ثلاثة وهي جمع مطلق ولهذا يتقدمهما الإمام ويصطفان خلفه. ولهما: إن الجمع المطلق شرط انعقاد الجمعة في حق كل واحد منهم وشرط جواز صلاة كل واحد منهم ينبغي أن يكون سواه، فيحصل هذا الشرط ثم يصلي ولا يحصل هذا الشرط إلا إذا كان سوى الإمام ثلاثة إذ لو كان مع الإمام اثنان لم يوجد في حق كل واحد منهم بخلاف سائر الصلوات لأن الجماعة فيها ليست بشرط . كذا في البدائع. أطلق الثلاثة فشمل العبيد والمسافرين والمرضى. والأميين والخرسى لصلاحيتهم للإمامة في الجمعة أما لكل واحد أو لمن هو مثل حالهم في الأمي والأخرس فصلحا أن يقتديا بمن فوقهما . كذا في المحيط. ولا يرد عليه النساء والصبيان فإن الجمعة لا تصح بهم وحدهم لعدم صلاحيتهم للإمامة فيها بحال لأن النساء خرجن بالتاء في ثلاثة أي ثلاثة رجال وكذا الصبي لأنه ليس برجل كامل والمطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل . وشمل ثلاثة غير الثلاثة الذين حضروا الخطبة لما في التجنيس وغيره : إذا خطب بحضره جماعة ثم نفروا وجاء آخرون لم يشهدوا الخطبة فصلي : الجمعة أجزأهم . بهم
He said: (And the congregation: they are three) i.e., the condition for its validity is that three or more pray with the imam, due to the consensus of scholars that congregation is necessary. They only differed on the amount: what the author mentioned is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: two besides the imam, because they two with the imam are three, and it is an absolute gathering; for this reason the imam leads them and they stand in rows behind him. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): The absolute gathering is a condition for the validity of Friday prayer for each one of them, and the condition for the permissibility of the prayer of each one should be other than him; so this condition is fulfilled then he prays, and this condition is only fulfilled if besides the imam there are three, because if there were two with the imam, it would not be found with respect to each one of them, unlike other prayers because congregation in them is not a condition. That is in al-Bada'i'. The three is absolute, so it includes slaves, travelers, and the sick. Also the illiterate and the mute, because they are fit to lead Friday prayer. ... Women and boys are not included because Friday prayer is not valid with them alone, due to their unfitness for leading it; because women are excluded by the ta in 'three', meaning three men, and likewise a boy is not a complete man, and the absolute is restricted to the complete. And 'three' includes other than the three who attended the khutbah, as in al-Tajnis: if he gave the khutbah in the presence of a congregation, then they left and others came who did not attend the khutbah, and he prayed Friday, it suffices for them.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the minimum congregation size for Friday prayer. The matn states that the congregation is three (besides the imam), which is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf holds that two suffice. The reasoning is that the absolute gathering (jama'ah) requires at least three persons total; for each person to be in a congregation, there must be at least three others besides himself. The text also clarifies who counts: slaves, travelers, sick, illiterate, and mute are included because they can lead Friday prayer under certain conditions. Women and boys are excluded because the term 'thalathah' (three) grammatically refers to males. Additionally, the three are not required to have attended the khutbah; if some leave and others come, the prayer is valid for the newcomers.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama'ah): The congregation required for Friday prayer; a group including the imam and followers.
ثلاثة (thalathah): Three men besides the imam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three followers besides the imam
C) One follower besides the imam
D) Forty followers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires at least three male followers besides the imam for Friday prayer; this is the mufta bihi view.

The Ruling on the Muraqqi: Hasanah not Bid'ah
Refutation of bid'ah claim for muraqqi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the muraqqi and explain the qiyas-based proof that it is a commendable practice (hasanah).

Core Idea
The muraqqi's recitation during Friday sermon is not a bid'ah: it is a hasanah supported by prophetic analogy.

Some have claimed that the practice of having an assistant (muraqqi) recite a verse when the khatib appears for the Friday sermon is an innovation (bid'ah). In this passage, the Hanafi scholar Ibn Nujaym refutes this claim, showing that the practice is actually commendable (hasanah). He bases his argument on the verse urging blessings on the Prophet, the hadith emphasizing attentive listening, and importantly, a qiyas on the Prophet's own action during the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
The passage opens by noting that some consider the muraqqi a bid'ah because it arose after the early generation. Recognize this as the opposing view.
The phrase 'حدث بعد الصدر الأول' indicates the temporal origin objection.
2
Understand the author's first two proofs
The author cites the verse (33:56) encouraging blessings on the Prophet, especially on Friday, and the hadith stressing attentive listening (insat). These provide general encouragement for the practice.
These proofs show the practice aligns with established recommendations.
3
Analyze the qiyas proof
The author draws an analogy (qiyas) from the Prophet's action at Mina during the Farewell Pilgrimage, where he commanded someone to ask people to listen. The muraqqi serves the same function, so the act is recommended for the khatib.
The key is that the Prophet's action is a precedent; the muraqqi's role is not a new invention.
4
Conclude the ruling
Based on these proofs, the practice is not a bid'ah but a hasanah (commendable). The author explicitly states: 'فلم يدخل ذكر للخبر في حين البدعة أصلاً' (the report's mention does not enter it at all; it is originally not a bid'ah).
The ruling is sunnah ghayr muakkadah according to later Hanafi jurists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدث بعد الصدر الأول قيل لكنها حسنة لحث الآية على ما يندب لكل أحد من إكثار الصلاة والسلام على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا سيما في ها اليوم وكحث الخبر على تأكد الإنصات المفوت تركه لفصل الجمعة بل والموقع في الإثم عند الأكثرين من العلماء وأقول : يستدل لذلك أيضاً بأنه أنه أمر من يستنصت له الناس عند إرادته خطب منى في حجة الوداع، فقياسه يندب للخطيب أمر غيره بأن يستنصت له الناس وهذا هو شأن المرقي فلم يدخل ذكر للخبر في حين البدعة أصلاً اه
It occurred after the early generation; it was said but it is good (hasanah) due to the verse urging what is recommended for everyone: abundant blessings and peace on the Messenger of Allah, especially on this day, and due to the hadith emphasizing attentive listening, the neglect of which causes loss of the virtue of Friday, and even places one in sin according to most scholars. And I say: evidence for that is also that he (the Prophet) commanded someone to ask people to listen when he intended to give the sermon at Mina during the Farewell Pilgrimage. By analogy, it is recommended for the khatib to command someone else to ask people to listen, and this is the role of the muraqqi. So the report's mention does not enter it at all; it is originally not a bid'ah.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage responds to a claim that the practice of having a muraqqi (an assistant who recites a verse to call people to listen) is a bid'ah. The author argues that it is actually a commendable practice (hasanah). First, the verse (33:56) encourages sending blessings on the Prophet, especially on Friday. Second, the hadith stresses attentive listening during the sermon. Third, the Prophet himself at Mina commanded someone to call for silence, so by qiyas, the khatib may appoint someone to do the same. Therefore, the muraqqi's role is not a bid'ah but a praiseworthy innovation based on sound principles.

Key Terms
مرقي (muraqqi): An assistant who recites a verse or calls for attention when the khatib emerges from the makhda (chamber) to the minbar.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religion; the author argues this practice is not a bid'ah because it has a basis in the sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is a bid'ah and prohibited
B) It is permissible and commendable (hasanah)
C) It is obligatory
D) It is disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
The muraqqi is a commendable practice (hasanah) based on prophetic analogy, not a blameworthy innovation.

The Necessity of Intention (Qasd) in the Friday Sermon
Explains the requirement of intention for the Friday khutbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that intention is required for the Friday khutbah and distinguish between accidental dhikr and deliberate khutbah.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah is valid only when performed with deliberate intention; accidental speech never substitutes.

The Friday sermon is a distinctive act of worship that requires more than mere words. In this lesson, we examine a key condition: the khutbah must be intended as such. A sneeze on the minbar, even if it contains dhikr, does not fulfill the obligation. The evidence lies in the Quranic command to hasten to the remembrance of Allah, which implies a deliberate act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The Friday khutbah is wajib. A condition for its validity is that it be performed with intention (qasd). Accidental utterances do not count.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 62:9: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' The khutbah is considered a form of dhikr (remembrance).
The verse's command implies a deliberate act of worship.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse commands hastening to dhikr. The scholars interpret 'dhikr' here as the khutbah. Since the khutbah is a specific act of worship, it must be intended; accidental utterances are not 'hastening to dhikr' in the required sense.
This is a zanni (speculative) dalala, but sufficient for wujub.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Abu Hanifah that accidental dhikr (like saying al-hamdu lillah after a sneeze) would suffice. However, the relied-upon view is that intention is necessary.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the view requiring intention.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is that intention is required. Accidental utterances do not substitute for the khutbah.
This is the position of the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة الجمعة
وصلى
بهم .
إلى إمام فعال أحوج منكم إلى إمام ،قوال، وستأتيكم الخطب بعد وأستغفر الله لي ولكم ونزل ولم ينكر عليه أحد منهم فكان إجماعاً. وارتج بالتخفيف على الأصح أي استغلق عليه الخطبة فلم يقدر على إتمامها كذا في المغرب ومراد عثمان بقوله «إنكم إلى إمام إلى آخره» أن الخلفاء الذين يأتون بعد الخلفاء الراشدين تكون على كثرة المقال مع قبح الفعال فأنا وإن لم أكن قوالاً مثلهم فأنا على الخير دون الشر، فأما أن يريد بهذا القول تفضيل نفسه على الشيخين فلا. كذا في النهاية : قيدنا الخطبة بالمفروضة لأن المسنونة لا يكفي فيها مطلقه بل لا بد أن يأتي بما قدمناه . وقيدنا بالقصد لأنه لو عطس على المنبر فقال الحمد لله على عطاسه لا ينوب عن الخطبة عند أبي حنيفة أيضاً كما في التسمية على الذبيحة وعن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى أنه يجزئه، والفرق على هذه الرواية وهو أن المأمور به في الخطبة الذكر مطلقاً لقوله تعالى فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله ﴾ [الجمعة: ۹] وقد وجد وفي باب الذبيحة المأمور الذكر عليه وذلك بأن يقصده والأول أصح . كذا في التنجيس
حدث بعد الصدر الأول قيل لكنها حسنة لحث الآية على ما يندب لكل أحد من إكثار الصلاة والسلام على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا سيما في ها اليوم وكحث الخبر على تأكد الإنصات المفوت تركه
لفضل الجمعة بل والموقع في الإثم عند الأكثرين من العلماء وأقول : يستدل لذلك أيضاً بأنه أنه أمر من يستنصت له الناس عند إرادته خطب منى في حجة الوداع، فقياسه يندب للخطيب أمر
غيره بأن يستنصت له الناس وهذا هو شأن المرقي فلم يدخل ذكر للخبر في حين البدعة أصلاً اه
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Friday Prayer. And he led them in prayer. To an imam who is active, you are more in need of an imam who is a speaker, and sermons will come to you after, and I seek forgiveness from Allah for myself and for you, and he descended, and none of them denied it, so it was consensus. And it became difficult (irtajja) with lightening (at-takhfif) according to the most correct, meaning the khutbah became locked for him and he could not complete it; thus in al-Mughrib. And the meaning of Uthman's statement 'You are more in need of an imam...' is that the caliphs who come after the rightly-guided caliphs will have much speech with bad deeds. So even if I am not a speaker like them, I am upon goodness and not evil. He did not intend by this statement to prefer himself over the two shaykhs. Thus in an-Nihayah. We restricted the khutbah to the obligatory one, because for the supererogatory, the absolute does not suffice, but rather one must bring what we have mentioned. And we restricted it with intention because if he sneezes on the minbar and says 'al-hamdu lillah' for his sneeze, it does not substitute for the khutbah according to Abu Hanifah as well, like saying 'bismillah' over the slaughter. And from Abu Hanifah in another narration that it suffices him. The difference according to this narration is that what is commanded in the khutbah is dhikr absolutely, due to His statement 'so hasten to the remembrance of Allah' [al-Jumu'ah:9], and it was found. And in the chapter of slaughter, the commanded is dhikr upon it, and that is by intending it, and the first is more correct. Thus in at-Tanjis. An innovation occurred after the first generation; it was said but it is good because the verse encourages what is recommended for everyone: increasing prayers and peace upon the Messenger of Allah, especially on this day, and because the hadith emphasizes the obligation of listening, the abandonment of which causes the loss of the virtue of Friday, and even places one in sin according to most scholars. And I say: one can also deduce for that that he (the Prophet) commanded someone to make the people listen when he intended to deliver the sermon of Mina during the Farewell Pilgrimage. By analogy, it is recommended for the khatib to command someone else to make the people listen, and this is the role of the mu'adhdhin. So the mention of the hadith was not introduced into the innovation at all. End.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions of the Jumu'ah khutbah. The author begins by recounting an incident from the time of Caliph Uthman, who after being unable to complete the khutbah due to a stammer, mentioned that people would need a talkative imam. The author explains that Uthman was not praising himself but rather describing the future caliphs. Then the author states two conditions: first, the khutbah must be the obligatory Friday khutbah, not a supererogatory one; second, it must be intended. If the imam sneezes and says 'al-hamdu lillah', it does not count as the khutbah because it was not intended as such. This is based on the verse 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' and a similar ruling in slaughtering where one must intend. There is a narration from Abu Hanifah that it would suffice, but the first view is more correct. The passage then discusses a later practice (bid'ah) of sending blessings on the Prophet during the khutbah, which the author defends as good because it is recommended and because the Prophet commanded silence during the khutbah. The author analogizes that the khatib should appoint someone to enforce silence, like the mu'adhdhin. The key ruling is that the khutbah must be a deliberate act of dhikr, and accidental utterances do not fulfill it.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon, which is wajib and must be intended as dhikr.
القصد (al-qasd): Intention; the act of deliberately performing the khutbah as an act of worship.
عطس (atasa): To sneeze; used in the example of accidental dhikr during the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because it was not intended as part of the khutbah.
C) Yes, because it is similar to saying bismillah over a slaughter.
D) No, because sneezing invalidates the khutbah entirely.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah requires deliberate intention; accidental utterances, even if they contain dhikr, do not fulfill the obligation.

The Required Number for Jumu'ah: Three Besides the Imam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Jumu'ah congregation number with expansion on eligible participants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the minimum number of participants in Jumu'ah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires three men besides the imam; each must have two others to form a valid congregation.

When praying Jumu'ah, the presence of a congregation is essential. But how many people are needed for the prayer to be valid? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer, with an internal disagreement between the founding imams. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the majority position and the practical implications of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
The core question is: what is the minimum number of participants (excluding the imam) required for a valid Jumu'ah prayer? Note that the imam is not counted as part of the congregation.
The dispute is only on the number; all agree congregation is necessary.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani require three persons besides the imam. Abu Yusuf holds that two besides the imam suffice.
These are both within the Hanafi school: an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Proof of Each
Abu Hanifah and Muhammad argue that the condition of congregation must be fulfilled for each individual follower: each must have at least two others besides himself. With two followers, each has only one other, so the condition fails. Abu Yusuf argues that a group exists with three total (imam +2), and that group (jamm' mutlaq) suffices.
The proof text in al-Bada'i' emphasizes 'in respect to each one of them.'
4
Examine the Scope: Who Counts?
The three men may be slaves, travelers, sick, illiterate, or mute, as they can lead or follow in Jumu'ah. Women and children are excluded because Jumu'ah is not valid with them alone and they cannot lead.
The absolute word 'three' applies to those fit for leadership or following in Jumu'ah.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Practical Consequences
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad: three besides imam. So if only two men attend besides the imam, Jumu'ah is invalid and Dhuhr must be prayed.
This is the view adopted by later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Kasani, al-Marghinani).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والجماعة وهم ثلاثة) أي شرط صحتها أن يصلي مع الإمام ثلاثة فأكثر لإجماع العلماء على أنه لا بد فيها من الجماعة كما في البدائع. وإنما اختلفوا في مقدارها فما ذكره المصنف قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : اثنان سوى الإمام لأنهما مع الإمام ثلاثة وهي جمع مطلق ولهذا يتقدمهما الإمام ويصطفان خلفه. ولهما: إن الجمع المطلق شرط انعقاد الجمعة في حق كل واحد منهم وشرط جواز صلاة كل واحد منهم ينبغي أن يكون سواه، فيحصل هذا الشرط ثم يصلي ولا يحصل هذا الشرط إلا إذا كان سوى الإمام ثلاثة إذ لو كان مع الإمام اثنان لم يوجد في حق كل واحد منهم بخلاف سائر الصلوات لأن الجماعة فيها ليست بشرط . كذا في البدائع. أطلق الثلاثة فشمل العبيد والمسافرين والمرضى. والأميين والخرسى لصلاحيتهم للإمامة في الجمعة أما لكل واحد أو لمن هو مثل حالهم في الأمي والأخرس فصلحا أن يقتديا بمن فوقهما . كذا في المحيط. ولا يرد عليه النساء والصبيان فإن الجمعة لا تصح بهم وحدهم لعدم صلاحيتهم للإمامة فيها بحال لأن النساء خرجن بالتاء في ثلاثة أي ثلاثة رجال وكذا الصبي لأنه ليس برجل كامل والمطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل . وشمل ثلاثة غير الثلاثة الذين حضروا الخطبة لما في التجنيس وغيره : إذا خطب بحضره جماعة ثم نفروا وجاء آخرون لم يشهدوا الخطبة فصلي : الجمعة أجزأهم . بهم
His statement: (And the congregation is three people) meaning its condition of validity is that three or more pray with the imam, due to the consensus of scholars that congregation is necessary in it, as in al-Bada'i'. They only differed on its quantity. What the author mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: two besides the imam, because they, with the imam, are three and it is an absolute group, and for this reason the imam leads them forward and they stand in rows behind him. And their (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad's) argument: The absolute group is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah in respect to each one of them, and the condition for the permissibility of the prayer of each one of them should be something other than himself. So this condition is obtained, then he prays, and this condition is not obtained unless besides the imam there are three, because if there were two with the imam, it would not exist in respect to each one of them, unlike other prayers because congregation in them is not a condition. Thus in al-Bada'i'. He released the word 'three' so it includes slaves, travelers, and sick. And the illiterate and the mute because of their suitability for leading the Jumu'ah prayer, either for each one or for those like their condition; the illiterate and the mute are suitable to follow someone above them. Thus in al-Muhit. And women and children are not excluded because Jumu'ah is not valid with them alone due to their unsuitability for leading it in any way, because women are excluded by the feminine ending in 'three', meaning three men, and similarly the boy because he is not a complete man, and the absolute applies to the complete. And it includes three other than the three who attended the khutbah, as in at-Tajnish and others: If he delivers the khutbah in the presence of a group, then they disperse and others come who did not attend the khutbah, then he prays Jumu'ah with them, it suffices them.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum number of participants required for a valid Jumu'ah prayer. The author states that it is a condition of validity that at least three persons (besides the imam) pray with the imam. This is based on scholarly consensus that congregation is necessary for Jumu'ah. The disagreement is on the number: Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani say three, while Abu Yusuf says two (making three total including the imam). Their reasoning: for Jumu'ah, the congregation is not just recommended but a condition (shart) for the validity of the prayer of each individual. To have a valid congregation, each person must have at least two others besides himself; thus with two followers, each has only one other follower, so the condition is not met. Abu Yusuf argues that the existence of a group (jamm' mutlaq) suffices, and two followers plus imam make three. The author adopts the view of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. Furthermore, the requirement of three men includes slaves, travelers, the ill, illiterate, and mute, as they are fit to lead Jumu'ah for their own kind. Women and children are excluded because Jumu'ah is not valid with them alone and they cannot lead. The passage also notes that if those who attended the khutbah leave and others come who did not hear it, the prayer with the new group is valid as long as there are three men.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): The group of followers praying behind an imam; for Jumu'ah, a minimum of three besides the imam is required.
الثلاثة (ath-thalathah): Three men, excluding the imam, who are fit to lead Jumu'ah, i.e., free, adult, sane males.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, how many people (excluding the imam) are required for a valid Jumu'ah prayer?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
For a valid Jumu'ah, the Hanafi school requires at least three men (free, adult, sane) besides the imam, based on the condition of congregation for each individual.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
