Ruling if Congregation Leaves Before Imam's Sajdah
Explains when the congregation's departure invalidates Jumu'ah, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding when the congregation's departure invalidates Jumu'ah, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The congregation is a condition for performance, not the opening takbir — which determines if Jumu'ah remains valid if they leave early.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does the congregation need to be present at the moment of the opening takbir, or throughout the prayer's performance? The answer determines whether Jumu'ah is invalidated if the followers leave after the takbir but before the imam's first sajdah. We will explore the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Abu Hanifah holds that the congregation is a condition for performance (ada'), tied to the first sajdah. The Sahibayn hold it is a condition for the opening takbir (tahrimah).
2
Identify the practical difference
If followers leave after takbir but before sajdah: according to Abu Hanifah, Jumu'ah is invalid and must be prayed as zuhr; according to the Sahibayn, it remains valid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
3
Follow Abu Hanifah's proof
Requiring congregation at the takbir would cause hardship due to the need for simultaneous takbirs. By consensus, it is not a condition for the takbir, as followers can join later.
Impossibility argument.
4
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
They analogize the imam to the follower: since the congregation is a condition for the follower's takbir, it should be for the imam as well.
Qiyas.
5
Determine the relied-upon position
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifah's view, as it avoids hardship and is supported by the consensus that the takbir does not require simultaneous participation.
As stated in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن نفروا قبل سجوده (بطلت بيان لكون الجماعة شرط انعقاد الأداء لا شرط انعقاد التحريمة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما شرط انعقاد التحريمة وفائدته أنهم لو نفروا بعد التحريمة قبل تقييد الركعة بالسجدة فسدت الجمعة ويستقبل الظهر عنده، وعندهما يتم الجمعة لأنها شرط انعقاد التحريمة في حق المقتدي فكذا في حق الإمام والجامع أن تحريمة الجمعة . إذا صحت صح بناء الجمعة عليها، ولهذا لو أدركه إنسان في التشهد صلى الجمعة عنده وهو قول أبي يوسف إلا أن محمداً تركه هنا لما سيأتي ولأبي حنيفة أن الجماعة في حق الإمام لو جعلت شرط انعقاد التحريمة لأدى إلى الحرج لأن تحريمته حينئذ لا تنعقد بدون مشاركة الجماعة إياه فيها، وذا لا يحصل إلا أن تقع تكبيراتهم مقارنة لتكبيرة الإمام وأنه مما يتعذر مراعاته. وبالإجماع ليس بشرط فإنهم لو كانوا حضروا وكبر الإمام ثم كبروا صح تكبيره وصار شارعاً في ا في الصلاة وصحت مشاركتهم إياه فلم يجعل شرط انعقاد التحريمة لعدم الإمكان فجعلت شرط انعقاد الأداء وهو بتقييد الركعة بالسجدة لأن الأداء فعل والحاجة إلى كون الفعل أداء للصلاة وفعل الصلاة هو القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود، ولهذا لو حلف لا يصلي فما لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة لا يحنث، فإذا لم يقيدها لم يوجد الأداء فلم ينعقد فشرط دوام مشاركة الجماعة الإمام إلى الفراغ عن الأداء، ولا معتبر ببقاء النسوان والصبيان ولا بما دون الثلاث من الرجال لأن الجمعة لا تنعقد بهم. فلو قال «فإن نفر واحد منهم لكان أولى . قيد بقوله قبل سجوده أي الإمام لأنهم لو نفروا بعد سجوده فإنها لا تبطل عندنا خلافاً لزفر، بناء على أنها عنده شرط بقائها منعقدة إلى آخر الصلاة كالطهارة وستر العورة. وعندنا ليست بشرط للبقاء لما عرف في البدائع ومن فروع المسألة ما لو أحرم الإمام ولم يحرموا حتى قرأ وركع فأحرموا بعد ما ركع، فإن أدركوه في الركوع صحت الجمعة لوجود المشاركة في الركعة الأولى وإلا فلا لعدمها بخلاف المسبوق فإنه تبع للإمام فيكتفي بالانعقاد في حق الأصل لكونه بانياً على صلاته ولا يخفى أن مراد المصنف أنهم نفروا قبل سجوده ولم يعودوا قبل سجوده وإلا فلو نفروا قبله وعادوا إليه قبله فلا فساد كما في الخلاصة. وفيها : وإذا كبر الإمام ومعه قوم متوضئون فلم يكبروا معه حتى أحدثوا ثم جاء آخرون وذهب الأولون جاز استحساناً، ولو كانوا محدثين فكبر ثم جاء آخرون استقبل التكبير ا هـ .
His statement: (If they disperse before his sajdah, it is invalid) is a clarification that the congregation is a condition for the commencement of performance (inqi'ad al-ada') not a condition for the commencement of the tahrimah according to Abu Hanifah, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is a condition for the commencement of the tahrimah. The benefit of this is that if they dispersed after the tahrimah before tying the rak'ah with a sajdah, Jumu'ah becomes invalid and he (the imam) prays zuhr according to him (Abu Hanifah), while according to the two he completes Jumu'ah because it is a condition for the commencement of the tahrimah in respect to the follower, so too in respect to the imam. The principle is that if the tahrimah of Jumu'ah is valid, the building of Jumu'ah upon it is valid. For this reason, if someone catches up with him in the tashahhud, he prays Jumu'ah according to him (Abu Yusuf), but Muhammad omitted it here for what will come. According to Abu Hanifah: if the congregation in respect to the imam were made a condition for the commencement of the tahrimah, it would lead to difficulty because his tahrimah then would not be valid without the participation of the congregation with him in it, and this is not obtained unless their takbirs are simultaneous with the imam's takbir, which is difficult to observe. By consensus, it is not a condition; if they were present and the imam said takbir and then they said takbir, his takbir is valid and he becomes a starter in the prayer, and their participation with him is valid. So it was not made a condition for the commencement of the tahrimah due to impossibility, so it was made a condition for the commencement of performance, which is tying the rak'ah with a sajdah, because performance is an action and the need is for the action to be a performance of the prayer, and the actions of prayer are standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. For this reason, if someone swore he would not pray, as long as he does not tie the rak'ah with a sajdah, he does not break the oath. So if he does not tie it, performance does not exist, so it is not valid. So the condition is the continuation of the congregation's participation with the imam until the completion of the performance. And the remaining of women and children is not considered, nor those less than three men, because Jumu'ah is not valid with them. If he said 'if one of them dispersed' it would be more appropriate. He restricted with 'before his sajdah', i.e., the imam, because if they disperse after his sajdah, it does not invalidate according to us, contrary to Zufar, based on his view that it is a condition for its remaining valid until the end of the prayer, like purity and covering the 'awrah. According to us it is not a condition for remaining, as is known in al-Bada'i'. Among the branches of this issue: if the imam begins the tahrimah and they do not begin until he recited and bowed, then they begin after he bowed: if they catch him in the ruku', Jumu'ah is valid due to participation in the first rak'ah, otherwise not due to lack of it, contrary to the latecomer (masbuq) who is a follower of the imam, so commencement in the original suffices for him because he builds upon his prayer. And it is not hidden that the author's meaning is that they dispersed before his sajdah and did not return before his sajdah; otherwise if they dispersed before it and returned to him before it, there is no invalidation as in al-Khulasa. In it: If the imam says takbir and with him are people with wudu, but they do not say takbir with him until they break wudu, and then others come and the first go, it is permissible by istihsan. And if they were without wudu and he said takbir, then others come, he must repeat the takbir. End.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of the congregation leaving during the Jumu'ah prayer. The key issue is whether the congregation is a condition for the validity of the opening takbir (tahrimah) or for the performance (ada') after the takbir. Abu Hanifah holds that it is a condition for the performance (which is complete only with the sajdah that ties the rak'ah), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is a condition for the takbir itself. The practical difference: if the congregation leaves after the takbir but before the sajdah, Abu Hanifah says Jumu'ah is invalid and must be made up as zuhr; the two say it remains valid. Abu Hanifah argues that requiring congregation at the takbir would cause hardship since it requires simultaneous takbirs. Instead, it is required that the congregation continues until the performance (ada') is completed. The condition is that at least three men remain until the imam's sajdah; if they leave after the sajdah, the prayer is valid. This is contrary to Zufar, who requires it for the entire prayer. The passage also discusses a scenario where the followers join the prayer late: if they catch the imam in ruku' of the first rak'ah, Jumu'ah is valid. If they come after the imam has already bowed and they miss the ruku', they are considered latecomers and the ruling differs. Also, if followers delay their takbir until after the imam has bent, the prayer may be invalid if they miss the ruku'. The passage ends with a note from al-Khulasa about cases of istihsan.

Key Terms
التحريمة (at-tahrimah): The opening takbir that commences the prayer and makes worldly actions prohibited.
انعقاد الأداء (inqi'ād al-adā'): The commencement of the actual performance of the prayer, which is complete only with the sajdah that ties the rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, if the congregation leaves after the opening takbir but before the imam performs the sajdah of the first rak'ah, what is the ruling?
A) The Jumu'ah becomes invalid and must be prayed as zuhr.
B) The Jumu'ah remains valid as long as at least one remains.
C) The prayer is suspended until they return.
D) It becomes supererogatory (nafl).

Key Takeaway
The congregation is a condition for the performance of Jumu'ah, not the opening takbir, so if they leave before the first sajdah, Jumu'ah becomes invalid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Timing of General Permission for Jumu'ah
A ruling statement restricting the timing of the general permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that the general permission for Jumu'ah must be given before the khatib emerges and explain why this timing is necessary.

Core Idea
The general permission must precede the khatib's emergence — it is a condition, not a formality.

In the Hanafi school, the Jumu'ah prayer requires a general permission (al-idhn al-'amm) from the ruler or his deputy. But when exactly must this permission be granted? Our passage clarifies that it must be given before the khatib comes out of his chamber to deliver the khutbah. Learn why this timing matters and how it affects the validity of the Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's subject
Locate the term 'al-idhn al-amm' and understand it as the permission to hold Jumu'ah.
It is a condition for the prayer.
2
Determine the timing condition
Find the phrase 'before the khatib emerges' and note that this is the key restriction.
3
Contrast with current practice
The author criticizes the practice of giving permission after the khatib emerges. Understand why the correct timing is essential.
4
Apply to real scenario
Consider a modern Jumu'ah: the mu'adhdhin or official must announce the permission before the khatib steps out.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والإذن العام) قلت : لكن ينبغي تقييد جواز ذلك على مذهبنا بما قبل خروج الخطيب من مخدعه لا كما يفعل الآن، وقد كنت ذكرت ذلك الخطيب السليمية في صالحية دمشق فأمر المرقى بفعل ذلك قبل خروجه وهو مستمر إلى الآن والحمد الله تعالى
His statement: (And the general permission). I say: But it is appropriate to restrict the permissibility of that, according to our madhhab, to before the khatib emerges from his chamber, not as is done now. And I had mentioned that to the khatib as-Sulaymiyyah in Salihiyyah of Damascus, so he ordered the mu'adhdhin to do it before his emergence, and it continues until now, and praise be to Allah, the Exalted.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This brief passage comments on the requirement of 'general permission' (al-idhn al-'amm) for Jumu'ah. The general permission is the authority given by the ruler or his deputy for the Jumu'ah to be held. The author notes that according to the Hanafi school, this permission should be granted before the khatib (speaker) comes out of his chamber (makhda') to deliver the khutbah, contrary to the current practice where it is given later. He shares a personal anecdote: he mentioned this to a khatib in Damascus, and the khatib ordered the mu'adhdhin to announce the permission before his emergence, and this practice continues. This shows the importance of adhering to the correct timing of the permission according to the madhhab.

Key Terms
الإذن العام (al-idhn al-'amm): The general permission from the ruler or his representative for the Jumu'ah prayer to be held, which must be given before the khatib emerges.
الخطيب (al-khatib): The person delivering the Friday sermon; his emergence signals the start of the khutbah.
المخدع (al-makhda'): The chamber or room where the khatib prepares before coming out to deliver the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Before the khatib emerges from his chamber
C) At any time before the prayer starts
D) Only at the time of the Prophet's khutbah

Key Takeaway
The general permission for Jumu'ah is valid only if granted before the khatib emerges from his chamber.

Ruling on Congregation Leaving Before Imam's Sajdah in Jumu'ah
Explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation as a condition for tahrima vs. ada' in Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether congregation is a condition for the opening takbir or for performance in Jumu'ah, and evaluate the practical consequences of the dispute.

Core Idea
In Jumu'ah, congregation is a condition for performance (Abu Hanifa) or for the opening takbir (Sahibayn)—the dispute affects validity when people leave before sajdah.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the role of congregation (jama'ah) in the validity of Friday prayer. The matn states that if people disperse before the imam's prostration, the prayer is invalid. The commentator unpacks why: for Abu Hanifa, congregation is a condition for the performance of the prayer, while for his two disciples, it is a condition for the opening takbir itself. You will learn the proofs for each view and the practical difference when the congregation leaves early.

Guided Path
1
State the matn ruling
Identify the base ruling from the matn: if they disperse before the imam's prostration, Jumu'ah is invalid.
The matn is the foundation; the commentary explains the reasoning.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds congregation is a condition for performance (ada'), not for the opening takbir. The Sahibayn hold it is a condition for the opening takbir (tahrima).
Performance is defined as tying a rak'ah with a sajdah.
3
Follow the proof of the Sahibayn
They analogize between follower and imam: since the follower's takbir requires congregation, so does the imam's, because the takbir is the foundation of the prayer.
The common point is that a valid takbir allows building the prayer upon it.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
He argues that requiring congregation for the imam's takbir would necessitate simultaneous takbirs, causing hardship. It is impossible to ensure, so by consensus it is not a condition for the imam.
Followers can join late; the imam's takbir stands alone.
5
Note the thamara
If people leave after takbir but before sajdah: Abu Hanifa says Jumu'ah invalid, pray Dhuhr; Sahibayn say complete Jumu'ah.
Zufar adds a third view: congregation is a condition for continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن نفروا قبل سجوده (بطلت بيان لكون الجماعة شرط انعقاد الأداء لا شرط انعقاد التحريمة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما شرط انعقاد التحريمة وفائدته أنهم لو نفروا بعد التحريمة قبل تقييد الركعة بالسجدة فسدت الجمعة ويستقبل الظهر عنده، وعندهما يتم الجمعة لأنها شرط انعقاد التحريمة في حق المقتدي فكذا في حق الإمام والجامع أن تحريمة الجمعة . إذا صحت صح بناء الجمعة عليها، ولهذا لو أدركه إنسان في التشهد صلى الجمعة عنده وهو قول أبي يوسف إلا أن محمداً تركه هنا لما سيأتي ولأبي حنيفة أن الجماعة في حق الإمام لو جعلت شرط انعقاد التحريمة لأدى إلى الحرج لأن تحريمته حينئذ لا تنعقد بدون مشاركة الجماعة إياه فيها، وذا لا يحصل إلا أن تقع تكبيراتهم مقارنة لتكبيرة الإمام وأنه مما يتعذر مراعاته. وبالإجماع ليس بشرط فإنهم لو كانوا حضروا وكبر الإمام ثم كبروا صح تكبيره وصار شارعاً في ا في الصلاة وصحت مشاركتهم إياه فلم يجعل شرط انعقاد التحريمة لعدم الإمكان فجعلت شرط انعقاد الأداء وهو بتقييد الركعة بالسجدة لأن الأداء فعل والحاجة إلى كون الفعل أداء للصلاة وفعل الصلاة هو القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود، ولهذا لو حلف لا يصلي فما لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة لا يحنث، فإذا لم يقيدها لم يوجد الأداء فلم ينعقد فشرط دوام مشاركة الجماعة الإمام إلى الفراغ عن الأداء، ولا معتبر ببقاء النسوان والصبيان ولا بما دون الثلاث من الرجال لأن الجمعة لا تنعقد بهم. فلو قال «فإن نفر واحد منهم لكان أولى . قيد بقوله قبل سجوده أي الإمام لأنهم لو نفروا بعد سجوده فإنها لا تبطل عندنا خلافاً لزفر، بناء على أنها عنده شرط بقائها منعقدة إلى آخر الصلاة كالطهارة وستر العورة. وعندنا ليست بشرط للبقاء لما عرف في البدائع ومن فروع المسألة ما لو أحرم الإمام ولم يحرموا حتى قرأ وركع فأحرموا بعد ما ركع، فإن أدركوه في الركوع صحت الجمعة لوجود المشاركة في الركعة الأولى وإلا فلا لعدمها بخلاف المسبوق فإنه تبع للإمام فيكتفي بالانعقاد في حق الأصل لكونه بانياً على صلاته ولا يخفى أن مراد المصنف أنهم نفروا قبل سجوده ولم يعودوا قبل سجوده وإلا فلو نفروا قبله وعادوا إليه قبله فلا فساد كما في الخلاصة. وفيها : وإذا كبر الإمام ومعه قوم متوضئون فلم يكبروا معه حتى أحدثوا ثم جاء آخرون وذهب الأولون جاز استحساناً، ولو كانوا محدثين فكبر ثم جاء آخرون استقبل التكبير ا هـ . قوله : (والإذن العام) قلت : لكن ينبغي تقييد جواز ذلك على مذهبنا بما قبل خروج الخطيب من مخدعه لا كما يفعل الآن، وقد كنت ذكرت ذلك الخطيب السليمية في صالحية دمشق فأمر المرقى بفعل ذلك قبل خروجه وهو مستمر إلى الآن والحمد الله تعالى قوله : ( وإلا فلو نفروا قبله الخ) قال في النهر : هذا يفيد أنهم لو عادوا إليه بعد ما رفع رأسه من الركوع أنها تصح وليس هذا في الخلاصة، بل المذكور فيها أنهم لو جاؤوا قبل أن يرفع رأسه من الركوع جاز ولا بد منه لأنهم لو لم يفتتحوا معه وإنما أدركوا في
His saying: (If they disperse before his prostration) it is invalid. This is an explanation that the congregation is a condition for the validity of performance, not a condition for the validity of the opening takbir according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is a condition for the validity of the opening takbir. The benefit is that if they dispersed after the opening takbir before tying the rak'ah with a prostration, then the Jumu'ah is invalid and he prays Dhuhr according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to them, he completes the Jumu'ah because it (congregation) is a condition for the validity of the opening takbir with respect to the follower, and likewise with respect to the imam. The common point is that the opening takbir of Jumu'ah, if it is valid, the building of Jumu'ah upon it is valid. For this reason, if a person catches up with him in the tashahhud, he prays Jumu'ah according to him (Abu Hanifa), and this is the view of Abu Yusuf, except that Muhammad left it here for a reason to come. For Abu Hanifa, if congregation were made a condition for the validity of the opening takbir with respect to the imam, it would lead to hardship because his opening takbir then would not be valid without the participation of the congregation with him, and this is not achieved except that their takbirs be simultaneous with the imam's takbir, and that is impossible to observe. And by consensus, it is not a condition, for if they were present and the imam said takbir, then they said takbir, his takbir is valid and he becomes a starter of the prayer, and their participation with him is valid. So it was not made a condition for the validity of the opening takbir due to impossibility. So it was made a condition for the validity of performance, which is tying the rak'ah with a prostration, because performance is an action, and the need is for the action to be a performance of the prayer. The action of the prayer is standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. For this reason, if one swears not to pray, he is not considered to have broken his oath until he ties the rak'ah with a prostration. So if he does not tie it, performance does not occur, so it is not valid. So the condition is that the congregation continues with the imam until the completion of performance. And there is no consideration for the remaining of women and boys, nor for less than three men, because Jumu'ah is not valid with them. If he said 'if one of them dispersed' it would be more appropriate. He restricted with his saying 'before his prostration', i.e. the imam's, because if they dispersed after his prostration, it is not invalid according to us, contrary to Zufar, based on his view that it (congregation) is a condition for its remaining valid until the end of the prayer, like purity and covering the private parts. According to us, it is not a condition for continuity, as is known in al-Bada'i. Among the branches of the issue: if the imam said the opening takbir and they did not say takbir until he recited and bowed, and they said takbir after he bowed, if they catch him in the bowing, Jumu'ah is valid because participation in the first rak'ah occurred; otherwise not, because of lack of participation, unlike the latecomer, for he is a follower of the imam, so validity in the original suffices for him because he is building on his prayer. It is not hidden that the author's intent is that they dispersed before his prostration and did not return before his prostration; otherwise, if they dispersed before it and returned to him before it, there is no corruption, as in al-Khulasa. And in it: when the imam says takbir and with him are people with ablution, and they did not say takbir with him until they broke their ablution, and then others came and the first ones left, it is permissible by istihsan. If they were without ablution and then others came, he repeats the takbir. His saying: (and the general permission). I say: but it is appropriate to restrict the permissibility of that according to our school to before the khatib comes out of his compartment, not as is done now. I mentioned this to the khatib al-Salimiyya in Salihiyya of Damascus, and he ordered that it be done before his exit, and it continues till now, praise be to Allah. His saying: (and if they dispersed before him, etc.) It says in al-Nahr: this implies that if they returned to him after he raised his head from bowing, it is valid, but this is not in al-Khulasa. Rather, what is mentioned there is that if they came before he raised his head from bowing, it is permissible and inevitable because if they did not begin with him but only caught up in
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the role of congregation (jama'ah) in Jumu'ah prayer. The matn states: 'If they disperse before his prostration, it is invalid.' The commentator explains that for Abu Hanifa, congregation is a condition for the validity of the performance (ada') but not for the validity of the opening takbir (tahrima). For Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), it is a condition for the validity of the opening takbir. The practical difference (thamara) is that if people leave after the takbir but before tying the rak'ah with a prostration, Abu Hanifa considers the Jumu'ah invalid and they must pray Dhuhr, while the Sahibayn say they complete Jumu'ah. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that making congregation a condition for the imam's opening takbir would cause hardship because it would require simultaneous takbirs, which is impractical. He analogizes that if congregation were required for the takbir, then if a latecomer catches the imam in tashahhud, his Jumu'ah would be invalid, but it is valid according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad differs on that branch. The passage also discusses a branch case: if the imam begins and others do not join until after ruku', but they catch him in ruku', the Jumu'ah is valid because they participated in the first rak'ah. The author adds a personal note restricting a certain permission to before the khatib leaves his compartment. Finally, he cites a quote from al-Nahr about returning after the imam raises his head from ruku', clarifying that the Khulasa only allows it before raising the head.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer; its validity is disputed concerning the role of congregation.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): The group of worshippers praying behind the imam; in this context, their presence is a condition for Jumu'ah's validity.
شرط انعقاد الأداء (shart in'iqaad al-ada'): A condition for the validity of the performance of the prayer, as opposed to the validity of the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if people disperse after the imam's opening takbir but before he performs sajdah in the first rak'ah, what is the ruling?
A) The Jumu'ah is valid and they continue.
B) The Jumu'ah is invalid and they must pray Dhuhr.
C) The Jumu'ah is valid only if they return before sajdah.
D) The Jumu'ah is suspended until they return.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether congregation is a condition for the opening takbir or for performance in Jumu'ah; the practical ruling depends on which imam's view is followed, with Abu Hanifa's position being more widely relied upon due to practical feasibility.
